            <a href="/wiki/Salvadoran_col%C3%B3n" title="Salvadoran colón">

            </a>
            , but the colón is out of circulation.
            <span style="font-size: 120%;">

      <p>
       <b>
        El Salvador
       </b>
       (
       <span class="nowrap">
        <span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt">
         <a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">
          /
          <span style="border-bottom:1px dotted">
           <span title="/ɛ/: 'e' in 'dress'">
            ɛ
           </span>
           <span title="'l' in 'lie'">
            l
           </span>
          </span>
          <span style="border-bottom:1px dotted">
           <span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">
            ˈ
           </span>
           <span title="'s' in 'sigh'">
            s
           </span>
           <span title="/æ/: 'a' in 'bad'">
            æ
           </span>
           <span title="'l' in 'lie'">
            l
           </span>
           <span title="'v' in 'vie'">
            v
           </span>
           <span title="/ə/: 'a' in 'about'">
            ə
           </span>
           <span title="'d' in 'dye'">
            d
           </span>
           <span title="/ɔːr/: 'ar' in 'war'">
            ɔːr
           </span>
          </span>
          /
         </a>
        </span>
        <small class="nowrap">
         (
         <span class="unicode haudio">
          <span class="fn">
           <span style="white-space:nowrap">
            <a href="/wiki/File:En-us-El_Salvador.ogg" title="About this sound">
             <img alt="About this sound" data-file-height="20" data-file-width="20" height="11" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" width="11"/>
            </a>
           </span>
           <a class="internal" href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/1/13/En-us-El_Salvador.ogg" title="En-us-El Salvador.ogg">
            listen
           </a>
          </span>
         </span>
         )
        </small>
       </span>
       ;
       <small>
        Spanish:
       </small>
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        <a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Spanish" title="Help:IPA/Spanish">
         [el salβaˈðor]
        </a>
       </span>
       ), officially the
       <b>
        Republic of El Salvador
       </b>
       (
       <a href="/wiki/Spanish_language" title="Spanish language">
        Spanish
       </a>
       :
       <i>
        <span lang="es">
         República de El Salvador
        </span>
       </i>
       , literally "Republic of The Savior"), is the smallest and the most
       <a href="/wiki/Population_density" title="Population density">
        densely
       </a>
       populated country in
       <a href="/wiki/Central_America" title="Central America">
        Central America
       </a>
       . El Salvador's capital and largest city is
       <a href="/wiki/San_Salvador" title="San Salvador">
        San Salvador
       </a>
       . As of 2016
       <sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;">
        <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=El_Salvador&amp;action=edit">
         [update]
        </a>
       </sup>
       , the country had a population of approximately 6.34 million,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UN_WPP_3-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-UN_WPP-3">
         [3]
        </a>
       </sup>
       consisting largely of
       <a href="/wiki/Mestizo" title="Mestizo">
        Mestizos
       </a>
       of European and Indigenous American descent.
      </p>
      <p>
       El Salvador was for centuries inhabited by several
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mesoamerican" title="Mesoamerican">
        Mesoamerican
       </a>
       nations, especially the
       <a href="/wiki/Pipil_people" title="Pipil people">
        Cuzcatlecs
       </a>
       , as well as the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lenca" title="Lenca">
        Lenca
       </a>
       and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Maya_people" title="Maya people">
        Maya
       </a>
       . In the early 16th century, the
       <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Empire" title="Spanish Empire">
        Spanish Empire
       </a>
       conquered the territory, incorporating it into the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Viceroyalty_of_New_Spain" title="Viceroyalty of New Spain">
        Viceroyalty of New Spain
       </a>
       ruled from
       <a href="/wiki/Mexico_City" title="Mexico City">
        Mexico City
       </a>
       . In 1821, the country achieved independence from Spain as part of the
       <a href="/wiki/First_Mexican_Empire" title="First Mexican Empire">
        First Mexican Empire
       </a>
       , then further seceded, as part of the
       <a href="/wiki/Federal_Republic_of_Central_America" title="Federal Republic of Central America">
        Federal Republic of Central America
       </a>
       , in 1823. When the Republic dissolved in 1841, El Salvador became a sovereign nation, then formed a short-lived union with
       <a href="/wiki/Honduras" title="Honduras">
        Honduras
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Nicaragua" title="Nicaragua">
        Nicaragua
       </a>
       called the
       <a href="/wiki/Greater_Republic_of_Central_America" title="Greater Republic of Central America">
        Greater Republic of Central America
       </a>
       , which lasted from 1895 to 1898.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Boland2001_8-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Boland2001-8">
         [8]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IhrieOropesa2011_9-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-IhrieOropesa2011-9">
         [9]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Haskin2012_10-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Haskin2012-10">
         [10]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       From the late 19th to the mid-20th century, El Salvador endured chronic political and
       <a href="/wiki/Economic_stability" title="Economic stability">
        economic instability
       </a>
       characterized by coups, revolts, and a succession of
       <a href="/wiki/Authoritarianism" title="Authoritarianism">
        authoritarian
       </a>
       rulers. Persistent
       <a href="/wiki/Social_inequality" title="Social inequality">
        socioeconomic inequality
       </a>
       and civil unrest culminated in the devastating
       <a href="/wiki/Salvadoran_Civil_War" title="Salvadoran Civil War">
        Salvadoran Civil War
       </a>
       (1979–1992), which was fought between the military-led government and a coalition of left-wing
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Guerilla_warfare" title="Guerilla warfare">
        guerrilla
       </a>
       groups. The conflict ended with the
       <a href="/wiki/Chapultepec_Peace_Accords" title="Chapultepec Peace Accords">
        Chapultepec Peace Accords
       </a>
       . This negotiated settlement established a multiparty constitutional republic, which remains in place to this day.
      </p>
      <p>
       El Salvador's economy has historically been dominated by agriculture, beginning with the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Indigo_plant" title="Indigo plant">
        indigo plant
       </a>
       (
       <i>
        añil
       </i>
       in Spanish), the most important crop during the colonial period,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Montgomery1995_11-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Montgomery1995-11">
         [11]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Murray1997_12-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Murray1997-12">
         [12]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and followed thereafter by
       <a href="/wiki/Coffee" title="Coffee">
        coffee
       </a>
       , which by the early 20th century accounted for 90 percent of export earnings.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Boland2001b_13-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Boland2001b-13">
         [13]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Pearcy2006_14-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Pearcy2006-14">
         [14]
        </a>
       </sup>
       El Salvador has since reduced its dependence on coffee and embarked on diversifying the economy by opening up trade and financial links and expanding the manufacturing sector.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FoleyHapipi2005_15-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FoleyHapipi2005-15">
         [15]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Salvadoran_col%C3%B3n" title="Salvadoran colón">
        colón
       </a>
       , the official currency of El Salvador since 1892, was replaced by the
       <a href="/wiki/United_States_dollar" title="United States dollar">
        U.S. dollar
       </a>
       in 2001.
      </p>
      <p>
       As of 2010
       <sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;">
        <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=El_Salvador&amp;action=edit">
         [update]
        </a>
       </sup>
       , El Salvador ranks 12th among Latin American countries in terms of the Human Development Index and fourth in Central America (behind
       <a href="/wiki/Panama" title="Panama">
        Panama
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Costa_Rica" title="Costa Rica">
        Costa Rica
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Belize" title="Belize">
        Belize
       </a>
       ) due in part to ongoing rapid industrialisation.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16">
        <a href="#cite_note-16">
         [16]
        </a>
       </sup>
       However, the country continues to struggle with high rates of poverty, inequality, and crime.
      </p>
      <p>
      </p>

        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-18">

      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">
        Etymology
       </span>
      </h2>
      <table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Unreferenced" role="presentation">
       <tr>
        <td class="mbox-image">
         <div style="width:52px">
          <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg">
           <img alt="" data-file-height="399" data-file-width="512" height="39" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" width="50"/>
          </a>
         </div>
        </td>
        <td class="mbox-text">
         <div class="mbox-text-span">
          This section
          <b>
           does not
           <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources">
            cite
           </a>
           any
           <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">
            sources
           </a>
          </b>
          .
          <span class="hide-when-compact">
           Please help
           <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=El_Salvador&amp;action=edit">
            improve this section
           </a>
           by
           <a href="/wiki/Help:Introduction_to_referencing_with_Wiki_Markup/1" title="Help:Introduction to referencing with Wiki Markup/1">
            adding citations to reliable sources
           </a>
           . Unsourced material may be challenged and
           <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability#Burden_of_evidence" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">
            removed
           </a>
           .
          </span>
          <small>
           <i>
            (August 2016)
           </i>
          </small>
          <small class="hide-when-compact">
           <i>
            (
            <a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">
             Learn how and when to remove this template message
            </a>
            )
           </i>
          </small>
         </div>
        </td>
       </tr>
      </table>
      <p>
       Conquistador
       <a href="/wiki/Pedro_de_Alvarado" title="Pedro de Alvarado">
        Pedro de Alvarado
       </a>
       named the new province for
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jesus_Christ" title="Jesus Christ">
        Jesus Christ
       </a>
       –
       <i>
        El Salvador
       </i>
       ("The Savior"). The full name was "
       <i>
        <span lang="es">
         Provincia De Nuestro Señor Jesus Cristo, El Salvador Del Mundo
        </span>
       </i>
       " ("Province of our Lord Jesus Christ, the Savior of the World"), which was subsequently abbreviated to "
       <i>
        <span lang="es">
         El Salvador
        </span>
       </i>
       " (The Savior).
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="History">
        History
       </span>
      </h2>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Prehistoric">
        Prehistoric
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Toma2.gif">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="541" data-file-width="623" height="191" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/Toma2.gif/220px-Toma2.gif" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/Toma2.gif/330px-Toma2.gif 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/Toma2.gif/440px-Toma2.gif 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Toma2.gif" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Excavation of a
         <a href="/wiki/Megatherium" title="Megatherium">
          Megatherium
         </a>
         in the Tomayate site
         <a href="/wiki/Apopa" title="Apopa">
          Apopa
         </a>
         .
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Toma4.gif">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="418" data-file-width="596" height="154" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/Toma4.gif/220px-Toma4.gif" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/Toma4.gif/330px-Toma4.gif 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/Toma4.gif/440px-Toma4.gif 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Toma4.gif" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Skull fossil of an ancient-horse in the Tomayate site
         <a href="/wiki/Apopa" title="Apopa">
          Apopa
         </a>
         .
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Tomayate&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Tomayate (page does not exist)">
        Tomayate
       </a>
       <span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;">
        (
        <a class="extiw" href="https://es.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tomayate" title="es:Tomayate">
         es
        </a>
        )
       </span>
       is a paleontological site located on the banks of the river of the same name in the municipality of
       <a href="/wiki/Apopa" title="Apopa">
        Apopa
       </a>
       . The site has produced abundant Salvadoran
       <a href="/wiki/Megafauna" title="Megafauna">
        megafauna
       </a>
       fossils belonging to the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pleistocene_epoch" title="Pleistocene epoch">
        Pleistocene epoch
       </a>
       . The paleontological site was discovered accidentally in 2000, and in the following year an excavation by the Museum of Natural History of El Salvador revealed not only several remnants of
       <a href="/wiki/Cuvieronius" title="Cuvieronius">
        Cuvieronius
       </a>
       , but also several other species of vertebrates. In the Tomayate site, they have recovered at least 19 species of vertebrates, including
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Giant_tortoises" title="Giant tortoises">
        giant tortoises
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Megatherium" title="Megatherium">
        Megatherium
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Glyptodon" title="Glyptodon">
        Glyptodon
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Toxodon" title="Toxodon">
        Toxodon
       </a>
       , extinct horses, paleo-llamas and especially a large number of skeletal remains of proboscis genus
       <a href="/wiki/Cuvieronius" title="Cuvieronius">
        Cuvieronius
       </a>
       . The Tomayate site stands out from most Central American
       <a href="/wiki/Pleistocene" title="Pleistocene">
        Pleistocene
       </a>
       deposits, being more ancient and much richer, which provides valuable information of the
       <a href="/wiki/Great_American_Interchange" title="Great American Interchange">
        Great American Interchange
       </a>
       , in which the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Central_American" title="Central American">
        Central American
       </a>
       isthmus landbridge played the title primordial role. At the same time, it is considered the richest vertebrate paleontological site in Central America and one of the largest accumulations of
       <a href="/wiki/Proboscidea" title="Proboscidea">
        proboscideans
       </a>
       in the Americas.
      </p>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/History_of_El_Salvador" title="History of El Salvador">
        History of El Salvador
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:ES_JoyadeCeren_06_2011_Estructura_9_Area_2_Tamazcal_2106.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="900" data-file-width="1350" height="200" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/ES_JoyadeCeren_06_2011_Estructura_9_Area_2_Tamazcal_2106.jpg/300px-ES_JoyadeCeren_06_2011_Estructura_9_Area_2_Tamazcal_2106.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/ES_JoyadeCeren_06_2011_Estructura_9_Area_2_Tamazcal_2106.jpg/450px-ES_JoyadeCeren_06_2011_Estructura_9_Area_2_Tamazcal_2106.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/ES_JoyadeCeren_06_2011_Estructura_9_Area_2_Tamazcal_2106.jpg/600px-ES_JoyadeCeren_06_2011_Estructura_9_Area_2_Tamazcal_2106.jpg 2x" width="300"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:ES_JoyadeCeren_06_2011_Estructura_9_Area_2_Tamazcal_2106.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Temazcal in Joya de Ceren.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Pre-Columbian">
        Pre-Columbian
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Cuzcatlan" title="Cuzcatlan">
        Cuzcatlan
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       Sophisticated civilization in El Salvador dates to its settlement by the indigenous
       <a href="/wiki/Lenca_people" title="Lenca people">
        Lenca people
       </a>
       ; theirs was the first and the oldest indigenous civilization to settle in El Salvador. The Lenca were succeeded by the
       <a href="/wiki/Olmec" title="Olmec">
        Olmecs
       </a>
       , who eventually also disappeared, leaving their monumental architecture in the form of the pyramids still extant in western El Salvador. The Maya arrived and settled in place of the Olmecs, but their numbers were greatly diminished when the
       <a href="/wiki/Lake_Ilopango" title="Lake Ilopango">
        Ilopango
       </a>
       supervolcano eruption caused a massive Mayan exodus out of what is now El Salvador.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Campbell1985_17-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Campbell1985-17">
         [17]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Centuries later they themselves were replaced by the
       <a href="/wiki/Pipil_people" title="Pipil people">
        Pipil people
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Nahuan_languages" title="Nahuan languages">
        Nahua
       </a>
       speaking groups
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Campbell1985_17-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-Campbell1985-17">
         [17]
        </a>
       </sup>
       who migrated from Mexico in the centuries before the European conquest and occupied the central and western regions. The Pipil were the last indigenous people to arrive in El Salvador.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Fowler1991_18-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Fowler1991-18">
         [18]
        </a>
       </sup>
       They called their territory
       <i>
        Kuskatan
       </i>
       , a
       <a href="/wiki/Pipil_language" title="Pipil language">
        Pipil
       </a>
       word
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Cárdenas1950_19-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Cárdenas1950-19">
         [19]
        </a>
       </sup>
       meaning
       <i>
        The Place of Precious Jewels
       </i>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Back-formation" title="Back-formation">
        backformed
       </a>
       into
       <a href="/wiki/Classical_Nahuatl" title="Classical Nahuatl">
        Classical Nahuatl
       </a>
       <i>
        Cōzcatlān
       </i>
       , and Hispanicized as
       <i>
        Cuzcatlán
       </i>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Baratta1951_20-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Baratta1951-20">
         [20]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Cárdenas1964_21-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Cárdenas1964-21">
         [21]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The people of El Salvador today are referred to as Salvadoran, while the term
       <i>
        Cuzcatleco
       </i>
       is commonly used to identify someone of Salvadoran heritage.
      </p>
      <p>
       In pre-Columbian times, the country was also inhabited by various other indigenous peoples, including the
       <a href="/wiki/Lenca_people" title="Lenca people">
        Lenca
       </a>
       , a
       <a href="/wiki/Lencan_languages#Classification" title="Lencan languages">
        Chilanga Lencan-speaking
       </a>
       group
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Campbell_22-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Campbell-22">
         [22]
        </a>
       </sup>
       who settled in the eastern highlands.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Tucker2008_23-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Tucker2008-23">
         [23]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Cuzcatlan was the larger domain until the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Spanish_conquest_of_the_Americas" title="Spanish conquest of the Americas">
        Spanish conquest
       </a>
       . Since El Salvador resided on the eastern edge of the Maya Civilization, the origins of many of El Salvador's ruins are controversial. However, it is widely agreed that Mayas likely occupied the areas around
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lake_Guija" title="Lake Guija">
        Lago de Guija
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Cihuat%C3%A1n" title="Cihuatán">
        Cihuatán
       </a>
       . Other ruins such as
       <a href="/wiki/Tazumal" title="Tazumal">
        Tazumal
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Joya_de_Cer%C3%A9n" title="Joya de Cerén">
        Joya de Cerén
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/San_Andr%C3%A9s,_El_Salvador" title="San Andrés, El Salvador">
        San Andrés
       </a>
       may have been built by the Pipil or the Maya or possibly both.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24">
        <a href="#cite_note-24">
         [24]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span id="European_contact_.281522.29">
       </span>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="European_contact_(1522)">
        European contact (1522)
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       By 1521, the indigenous population of the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mesoamerican" title="Mesoamerican">
        Mesoamerican
       </a>
       area had been drastically reduced by the smallpox epidemic that was spreading throughout the territory, although it had not yet reached pandemic levels in Cuzcatlán.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Peters2005_25-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Peters2005-25">
         [25]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Card2007_26-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Card2007-26">
         [26]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27">
        <a href="#cite_note-27">
         [27]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The first known visit by Spaniards to what is now Salvadoran territory was made by the Spanish admiral,
       <a href="/wiki/Andr%C3%A9s_Ni%C3%B1o" title="Andrés Niño">
        Andrés Niño
       </a>
       , who led a Spanish expedition to Central America. He disembarked in the
       <a href="/wiki/Gulf_of_Fonseca" title="Gulf of Fonseca">
        Gulf of Fonseca
       </a>
       on May 31, 1522, at
       <a href="/wiki/Meanguera_del_Golfo" title="Meanguera del Golfo">
        Meanguera island
       </a>
       , naming it Petronila,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Valdés2006_28-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Valdés2006-28">
         [28]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and then discovered
       <a href="/wiki/Jiquilisco_Bay" title="Jiquilisco Bay">
        Jiquilisco Bay
       </a>
       on the mouth of
       <a href="/wiki/Lempa_River" title="Lempa River">
        Lempa River
       </a>
       . The first indigenous people to have contact with the Spanish were the Lenca of eastern El Salvador.
      </p>
      <h4>
       <span id="Conquest_of_Cuzcatl.C3.A1n_.281524.E2.80.931525.29">
       </span>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Conquest_of_Cuzcatlán_(1524–1525)">
        Conquest of Cuzcatlán (1524–1525)
       </span>
      </h4>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Spanish_conquest_of_El_Salvador" title="Spanish conquest of El Salvador">
        Spanish conquest of El Salvador
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Pedro_de_Alvarado.JPG">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="800" data-file-width="580" height="234" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/Pedro_de_Alvarado.JPG/170px-Pedro_de_Alvarado.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/Pedro_de_Alvarado.JPG/255px-Pedro_de_Alvarado.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/Pedro_de_Alvarado.JPG/340px-Pedro_de_Alvarado.JPG 2x" width="170"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Pedro_de_Alvarado.JPG" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Spanish Conquistador
         <a href="/wiki/Pedro_de_Alvarado" title="Pedro de Alvarado">
          Pedro de Alvarado
         </a>
         .
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       In 1524, after participating in the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Conquest_of_Mexico" title="Conquest of Mexico">
        conquest of Mexico
       </a>
       , Spanish
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Conquistadors" title="Conquistadors">
        conquistadors
       </a>
       led by
       <a href="/wiki/Pedro_de_Alvarado" title="Pedro de Alvarado">
        Pedro de Alvarado
       </a>
       and his brother Gonzalo crossed the
       <a href="/wiki/Paz_River" title="Paz River">
        Rio Paz
       </a>
       (Peace River) from the area comprising the present Republic of Guatemala into what is now the Republic of El Salvador. The Spaniards were disappointed to discover that the indigenous
       <a href="/wiki/Pipil_people" title="Pipil people">
        Pipil people
       </a>
       had no gold or jewels like those they had found in Guatemala or Mexico, but recognized the richness of the land's volcanic soil.
      </p>
      <p>
       Pedro de Alvarado led the first incursion by Spanish forces to extend their dominion to the nation of
       <a href="/wiki/Cuzcatlan" title="Cuzcatlan">
        Cuzcatlan
       </a>
       (El Salvador), in June 1524.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NicholsPool2012_29-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-NicholsPool2012-29">
         [29]
        </a>
       </sup>
       When he arrived at the borders of the Cuzcatlan kingdom he saw that civilians had been evacuated. Cuzcatlec warriors moved to the coastal city of
       <a href="/wiki/Acajutla" title="Acajutla">
        Acajutla
       </a>
       and waited for Alvarado and his forces. Alvarado approached, confident that the result would be similar to what occurred in Mexico and Guatemala where the people believed the Spanish were gods. He thought he would easily defeat this new indigenous force since his Mexican allies and the Pipil of Cuzcatlan spoke a similar language.
      </p>
      <p>
       The Indigenous peoples of El Salvador did not see the Spanish as gods, but as foreign invaders. Alvarado saw that the Cuzcatan force outnumbered his Spanish soldiers and Mexican Indian allies. The Spanish withdrew and the Cuzcatlec army attacked, running behind them with war chants and shooting bow arrows. Alvarado had no choice but to fight to survive.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2016)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Alvarado described the Cuzcatlec soldiers in great detail as having shields made of colorful exotic feathers, a vest-like armor made of three inch cotton which arrows could not penetrate, and large spears. Both armies suffered many casualties, with a wounded Alvarado retreating and losing a lot of his men, especially among the Mexican Indian auxiliaries. Once his army had regrouped, Alvarado decided to head to the Cuzcatlan capital and again faced armed Cuzcatlec. Wounded, unable to fight and hiding in the cliffs, Alvarado sent his Spanish men on their horses to approach the Cuzcatlec to see if they would fear the horses, but they did not retreat, Alvarado recalls in his letters to Hernan Cortez.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2016)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The Cuzcatlec attacked again, and on this occasion stole Spanish weaponry. Alvarado retreated and sent Mexican Indian messengers to demand that the Cuzcatlec warriors return the stolen weapons and surrender to the Spanish king. The Cuzcatlec responded with the famous response, "If you want your weapons, come get them". As days passed, Alvarado, fearing an ambush, sent more Mexican Indian messengers to negotiate, but these messengers never came back and were presumably executed.
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Templo_tazumal.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2112" data-file-width="2816" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Templo_tazumal.jpg/220px-Templo_tazumal.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Templo_tazumal.jpg/330px-Templo_tazumal.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Templo_tazumal.jpg/440px-Templo_tazumal.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Templo_tazumal.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Tazumal" title="Tazumal">
          Tazumal
         </a>
         ruins in Santa Ana, El Salvador.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The Spanish efforts were firmly resisted by the indigenous people, including the Pipil and their Mayan-speaking neighbors. They defeated the Spaniards and what was left of their Mexican
       <a href="/wiki/Tlaxcala" title="Tlaxcala">
        Tlaxcala
       </a>
       Indian allies, forcing them to withdraw to Guatemala. After being wounded, Alvarado abandoned the war and appointed his brother,
       <a href="/wiki/Gonzalo_de_Alvarado" title="Gonzalo de Alvarado">
        Gonzalo de Alvarado
       </a>
       , to continue the task. Two subsequent expeditions (the first in 1525, followed by a smaller group in 1528) brought the Pipil under Spanish control, since the Pipil also were weakened by a regional epidemic of
       <a href="/wiki/Smallpox" title="Smallpox">
        smallpox
       </a>
       . In 1525, the conquest of Cuzcatlán was completed and the city of
       <a href="/wiki/San_Salvador" title="San Salvador">
        San Salvador
       </a>
       was established. The Spanish faced much resistance from the Pipil and were not able to reach eastern El Salvador, the area of the Lencas.
      </p>
      <p>
       In 1526 the Spanish founded the garrison town of
       <a href="/wiki/San_Miguel,_El_Salvador" title="San Miguel, El Salvador">
        San Miguel
       </a>
       , headed by another explorer and conquistador,
       <a href="/wiki/Luis_de_Moscoso_Alvarado" title="Luis de Moscoso Alvarado">
        Luis de Moscoso Alvarado
       </a>
       , nephew of Pedro Alvarado. Oral history holds that a Maya-Lenca crown princess, Antu Silan Ulap I, organized resistance to the conquistadors.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30">
        <a href="#cite_note-30">
         [30]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The kingdom of Lenca was alarmed by de Moscoso's invasion, and Antu Silan travelled from village to village, uniting all the Lenca towns in present-day El Salvador and Honduras against the Spaniards. Through surprise attacks and overwhelming numbers, they were able to drive the Spanish out of San Miguel and destroy the garrison.
      </p>
      <p>
       For ten years the Lencas prevented the Spanish from building a permanent settlement. Then the Spanish returned with more soldiers, including about 2,000 forced conscripts from indigenous communities in Guatemala. They pursued the Lenca leaders further up into the mountains of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Intibuc%C3%A1" title="Intibucá">
        Intibucá
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       Antu Silan Ulap eventually handed over control of the Lenca resistance to
       <a href="/wiki/Lempira_(Lenca_ruler)" title="Lempira (Lenca ruler)">
        Lempira
       </a>
       (also called Empira). Lempira was noteworthy among indigenous leaders in that he mocked the Spanish by wearing their clothes after capturing them and using their weapons captured in battle. Lempira fought in command of thousands of Lenca forces for six more years in El Salvador and Honduras until he was killed in battle. The remaining Lenca forces retreated into the hills. The Spanish were then able to rebuild their garrison town of San Miguel in 1537.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span id="Spanish_rule_.281525.E2.80.931821.29">
       </span>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Spanish_rule_(1525–1821)">
        Spanish rule (1525–1821)
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Proclama_de_libertad_(indep._Centroam%C3%A9rica).jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="800" data-file-width="1166" height="151" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/Proclama_de_libertad_%28indep._Centroam%C3%A9rica%29.jpg/220px-Proclama_de_libertad_%28indep._Centroam%C3%A9rica%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/Proclama_de_libertad_%28indep._Centroam%C3%A9rica%29.jpg/330px-Proclama_de_libertad_%28indep._Centroam%C3%A9rica%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/Proclama_de_libertad_%28indep._Centroam%C3%A9rica%29.jpg/440px-Proclama_de_libertad_%28indep._Centroam%C3%A9rica%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Proclama_de_libertad_(indep._Centroam%C3%A9rica).jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         A painting of the First Independence Movement celebration in San Salvador. At the center,
         <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Mat%C3%ADas_Delgado" title="José Matías Delgado">
          José Matías Delgado
         </a>
         .
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:MANUEL_JOSE_ARCE_PICTURE.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1013" data-file-width="570" height="302" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/MANUEL_JOSE_ARCE_PICTURE.jpg/170px-MANUEL_JOSE_ARCE_PICTURE.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/MANUEL_JOSE_ARCE_PICTURE.jpg/255px-MANUEL_JOSE_ARCE_PICTURE.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/MANUEL_JOSE_ARCE_PICTURE.jpg/340px-MANUEL_JOSE_ARCE_PICTURE.jpg 2x" width="170"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:MANUEL_JOSE_ARCE_PICTURE.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Manuel_Jos%C3%A9_Arce" title="Manuel José Arce">
          Manuel José Arce
         </a>
         joined the movement for independence from Spain, joining in the first Cry for Independence on November 5, 1811 in San Salvador.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       During the colonial period, El Salvador was part of the
       <a href="/wiki/Captaincy_General_of_Guatemala" title="Captaincy General of Guatemala">
        Captaincy General of Guatemala
       </a>
       , also known as the Kingdom of Guatemala (
       <a href="/wiki/Spanish_language" title="Spanish language">
        Spanish
       </a>
       :
       <i>
        <span lang="es">
         Reino de Guatemala
        </span>
       </i>
       ), created in 1609 as an administrative division of
       <a href="/wiki/New_Spain" title="New Spain">
        New Spain
       </a>
       . The Salvadoran territory was administered by the Mayor of Sonsonate, with San Salvador being established as an
       <i>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Intendancy" title="Intendancy">
         intendancia
        </a>
       </i>
       in 1786.
      </p>
      <p>
       Towards the end of 1811, a combination of internal and external factors motivated Central American elites to attempt to gain independence from the Spanish Crown. The most important internal factors were the desire of local elites to control the country's affairs free of involvement from Spanish authorities, and the long-standing Creole aspiration for independence. The main external factors motivating the independence movement were the success of the
       <a href="/wiki/French_Revolution" title="French Revolution">
        French
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/American_Revolution" title="American Revolution">
        American
       </a>
       revolutions in the 18th century, and the weakening of the Spanish Crown's military power as a result of the
       <a href="/wiki/Napoleonic_Wars" title="Napoleonic Wars">
        Napoleonic Wars
       </a>
       , with the resulting inability to control its colonies effectively.
      </p>
      <p>
       In November 1811 Salvadoran priest
       <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Mat%C3%ADas_Delgado" title="José Matías Delgado">
        José Matías Delgado
       </a>
       rang the bells of Iglesia La Merced in San Salvador, calling for insurrection and launching the
       <a href="/wiki/1811_Independence_Movement" title="1811 Independence Movement">
        1811 Independence Movement
       </a>
       . This insurrection was suppressed and many of its leaders were arrested and served sentences in jail. Another insurrection was launched in 1814, and again this insurrection was also suppressed.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span id="Independence_.281821.29">
       </span>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Independence_(1821)">
        Independence (1821)
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       In 1821 in light of unrest in Guatemala, Spanish authorities capitulated and signed the
       <a href="/wiki/Act_of_Independence_of_Central_America" title="Act of Independence of Central America">
        Act of Independence of Central America
       </a>
       , which released all of the Captaincy of Guatemala (comprising current territories of Guatemala, El Salvador, Honduras, Nicaragua and Costa Rica and the Mexican state of
       <a href="/wiki/Chiapas" title="Chiapas">
        Chiapas
       </a>
       ) from Spanish rule and declared its independence. In 1821, El Salvador joined Costa Rica, Guatemala, Honduras and Nicaragua in a union named the
       <a href="/wiki/Federal_Republic_of_Central_America" title="Federal Republic of Central America">
        Federal Republic of Central America
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       In early 1822, the authorities of the newly independent Central American provinces, meeting in Guatemala City, voted to join the newly constituted
       <a href="/wiki/First_Mexican_Empire" title="First Mexican Empire">
        First Mexican Empire
       </a>
       under
       <a href="/wiki/Agust%C3%ADn_de_Iturbide" title="Agustín de Iturbide">
        Agustín de Iturbide
       </a>
       . El Salvador resisted, insisting on autonomy for the Central American countries. A Mexican military detachment marched to
       <a href="/wiki/San_Salvador" title="San Salvador">
        San Salvador
       </a>
       and suppressed dissent, but with the fall of Iturbide on 19 March 1823, the army decamped back to Mexico. Shortly thereafter, the authorities of the provinces revoked the vote to join Mexico, deciding instead to form a federal union of the five remaining provinces. (Chiapas permanently joined Mexico at this juncture.)
      </p>
      <p>
       When the Federal Republic of Central America dissolved in 1841, El Salvador maintained its own government until it joined Honduras and Nicaragua in 1896 to form the
       <a href="/wiki/Greater_Republic_of_Central_America" title="Greater Republic of Central America">
        Greater Republic of Central America
       </a>
       , which dissolved in 1898.
      </p>
      <p>
       After the mid-19th century, the economy was based on coffee growing. As the world market for indigo withered away, the economy prospered or suffered as the world coffee price fluctuated. The enormous profits that
       <a href="/wiki/Coffee" title="Coffee">
        coffee
       </a>
       yielded as a monoculture export served as an impetus for the concentration of land into the hands of an
       <a href="/wiki/Oligarchy" title="Oligarchy">
        oligarchy
       </a>
       of just a few families.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31">
        <a href="#cite_note-31">
         [31]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Throughout the last half of the 19th century, a succession of
       <a href="/wiki/President" title="President">
        presidents
       </a>
       from the ranks of the Salvadoran oligarchy, nominally both
       <a href="/wiki/Conservatism" title="Conservatism">
        conservative
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Liberalism" title="Liberalism">
        liberal
       </a>
       , generally agreed on the promotion of coffee as the predominant
       <a href="/wiki/Cash_crop" title="Cash crop">
        cash crop
       </a>
       , the development of infrastructure (
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Railroad" title="Railroad">
        railroads
       </a>
       and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sea_port" title="Sea port">
        port facilities
       </a>
       ) primarily in support of the coffee trade, the elimination of communal landholdings to facilitate further coffee production, the passage of anti-
       <a href="/wiki/Vagrancy_(people)" title="Vagrancy (people)">
        vagrancy
       </a>
       laws to ensure that displaced
       <a href="/wiki/Peasant" title="Peasant">
        campesinos
       </a>
       and other rural residents provided sufficient
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Labour_(economics)" title="Labour (economics)">
        labor
       </a>
       for the coffee fincas (
       <a href="/wiki/Plantation" title="Plantation">
        plantations
       </a>
       ), and the suppression of rural discontent. In 1912, the national guard was created as a rural police force.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="20th_century">
        20th century
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Tom%C3%A1s_Regalado.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="239" data-file-width="150" height="239" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/0/07/Tom%C3%A1s_Regalado.jpg" width="150"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Tom%C3%A1s_Regalado.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Gen. Tomás Regalado
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       In 1898, Gen.
       <a href="/wiki/Tom%C3%A1s_Regalado_(Salvadoran_politician)" title="Tomás Regalado (Salvadoran politician)">
        Tomas Regalado
       </a>
       gained power by force, deposing
       <a href="/wiki/Rafael_Antonio_Guti%C3%A9rrez" title="Rafael Antonio Gutiérrez">
        Rafael Antonio Gutiérrez
       </a>
       and ruling as president until 1903. Once in office he revived the practice of presidents designating their successors. After serving his term, he remained active in the Army of El Salvador, and was killed July 11, 1906, at El Jicaro during a war against Guatemala. Until 1913 El Salvador was politically stable, with undercurrents of popular discontent. When President Dr.
       <a href="/wiki/Manuel_Enrique_Araujo" title="Manuel Enrique Araujo">
        Manuel Enrique Araujo
       </a>
       was killed in 1913, many hypotheses were advanced for the political motive of his murder.
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Civil_Ensign_of_El_Salvador.svg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="500" data-file-width="860" height="99" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/Civil_Ensign_of_El_Salvador.svg/170px-Civil_Ensign_of_El_Salvador.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/Civil_Ensign_of_El_Salvador.svg/255px-Civil_Ensign_of_El_Salvador.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/Civil_Ensign_of_El_Salvador.svg/340px-Civil_Ensign_of_El_Salvador.svg.png 2x" width="170"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Civil_Ensign_of_El_Salvador.svg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Dios, Union, Libertad (God, Unity, Liberty) El Salvador 1912 Flag.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Araujo's administration was followed by the Melendez-Quinonez dynasty that lasted from 1913 to 1927.
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pio_Romero_Bosque" title="Pio Romero Bosque">
        Pio Romero Bosque
       </a>
       , ex-Minister of the Government and a trusted collaborator of the dynasty, succeeded President
       <a href="/wiki/Jorge_Mel%C3%A9ndez" title="Jorge Meléndez">
        Jorge Meléndez
       </a>
       and in 1930 announced free elections, in which
       <a href="/wiki/Arturo_Araujo" title="Arturo Araujo">
        Arturo Araujo
       </a>
       came to power on March 1, 1931 in what was considered the country's first freely contested election. His government lasted only nine months before it was overthrown by junior military officers who accused his Labor Party of lacking political and governmental experience and of using its government offices inefficiently. President Araujo faced general popular discontent, as the people had expected economic reforms and the redistribution of land. There were demonstrations in front of the National Palace from the first week of his administration. His vice president and minister of war was Gen.
       <a href="/wiki/Maximiliano_Hern%C3%A1ndez_Mart%C3%ADnez" title="Maximiliano Hernández Martínez">
        Maximiliano Hernández Martínez
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       In December 1931, a
       <a href="/wiki/Coup_d%27%C3%A9tat" title="Coup d'état">
        coup d'état
       </a>
       organized by junior officers and led by Gen. Martínez started in the First Regiment of Infantry across from the National Palace in downtown San Salvador. Only the First Regiment of Cavalry and the National Police defended the presidency (the National Police had been on its payroll), but later that night, after hours of fighting, the badly outnumbered defenders surrendered to rebel forces.
      </p>
      <p>
       The Directorate, composed of officers, hid behind a shadowy figure,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32">
        <a href="#cite_note-32">
         [32]
        </a>
       </sup>
       a rich anti-Communist banker called Rodolfo Duke, and later installed the ardent fascist Gen. Martínez as president. The revolt was probably due to the army's discontent at not having been paid by President Araujo for some months. Araujo left the National Palace and unsuccessfully tried to organize forces to defeat the revolt.
      </p>
      <p>
       The U.S. Minister in El Salvador met with the Directorate and later recognized the government of Martínez, which agreed to hold presidential elections. He resigned six months prior to running for re-election, winning back the presidency as the only candidate on the ballot. He ruled from 1935 to 1939, then from 1939 to 1943. He began a fourth term in 1944, but resigned in May after a general strike. Martínez had said he was going to respect the Constitution, which stipulated he could not be re-elected, but he refused to keep his promise.
      </p>
      <p>
       From December 1931, the year of the coup that brought Martínez to power, there was brutal suppression of rural resistance. The most notable event was the February
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/1932_Salvadoran_peasant_uprising" title="1932 Salvadoran peasant uprising">
        1932 Salvadoran peasant uprising
       </a>
       , originally led by
       <a href="/wiki/Farabundo_Mart%C3%AD" title="Farabundo Martí">
        Farabundo Martí
       </a>
       and Abel Cuenca, and university students Alfonso Luna and Mario Zapata, but these leaders were captured before the planned insurrection. Only Cuenca survived; the other insurgents were killed by the government. After the capture of the movement leaders, the insurrection erupted in a disorganized and mob-controlled fashion, resulting in government repression that was later referred to as
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/1932_Salvadoran_peasant_uprising" title="1932 Salvadoran peasant uprising">
        La Matanza
       </a>
       (The Massacre), because tens of thousands of peasants died in the ensuing chaos on the orders of President Martinez.
      </p>
      <p>
       In the unstable political climate of the previous few years, the social activist and revolutionary leader
       <a href="/wiki/Farabundo_Mart%C3%AD" title="Farabundo Martí">
        Farabundo Martí
       </a>
       helped found the Communist Party of Central America, and led a Communist alternative to the Red Cross called International Red Aid, serving as one of its representatives. Their goal was to help poor and underprivileged Salvadorans through the use of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Marxist-Leninist" title="Marxist-Leninist">
        Marxist-Leninist
       </a>
       ideology (strongly rejecting
       <a href="/wiki/Stalinism" title="Stalinism">
        Stalinism
       </a>
       ). In December 1930, at the height of the country's economic and social depression, Martí was once again exiled due to his popularity among the nation's poor and rumors of his upcoming nomination for President the following year. Once Arturo Araujo was elected president in 1931, Martí returned to El Salvador, and along with Alfonso Luna and Mario Zapata began the movement that was later truncated by the military.
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Jose_Napoleon_Duarte.png">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="550" data-file-width="366" height="331" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Jose_Napoleon_Duarte.png/220px-Jose_Napoleon_Duarte.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Jose_Napoleon_Duarte.png/330px-Jose_Napoleon_Duarte.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/6/60/Jose_Napoleon_Duarte.png 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Jose_Napoleon_Duarte.png" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Napole%C3%B3n_Duarte" title="José Napoleón Duarte">
          José Napoleón Duarte
         </a>
         .
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       They helped start a guerrilla revolt of indigenous farmers. The government responded by
       <a href="/wiki/1932_Salvadoran_peasant_massacre" title="1932 Salvadoran peasant massacre">
        killing over 30,000 people
       </a>
       at what was to have been a "peaceful meeting" in 1932; this became known as La Matanza (The Slaughter). The peasant uprising against Martínez was crushed by the Salvadoran military ten days after it had begun. The Communist-led rebellion, fomented by collapsing coffee prices, enjoyed some initial success, but was soon drowned in a bloodbath. President Martínez, who had himself toppled an elected government only weeks earlier, ordered the defeated Martí shot after a perfunctory hearing.
      </p>
      <p>
       Historically, the high Salvadoran population density has contributed to tensions with neighboring
       <a href="/wiki/Honduras" title="Honduras">
        Honduras
       </a>
       , as land-poor Salvadorans emigrated to less densely populated Honduras and established themselves as squatters on unused or underused land. This phenomenon was a major cause of the
       <a href="/wiki/Football_War" title="Football War">
        1969 Football War
       </a>
       between the two countries.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33">
        <a href="#cite_note-33">
         [33]
        </a>
       </sup>
       As many as 130,000 Salvadorans were forcibly expelled or fled from Honduras.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34">
        <a href="#cite_note-34">
         [34]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Christian_Democratic_Party_(El_Salvador)" title="Christian Democratic Party (El Salvador)">
        Christian Democratic Party
       </a>
       (PDC) and the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/National_Conciliation_Party" title="National Conciliation Party">
        National Conciliation Party
       </a>
       (PCN) were active in Salvadoran politics from 1960 until 2011, when they were disbanded by the Supreme Court because they had failed to win enough votes in the 2004 presidential election;
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35">
        <a href="#cite_note-35">
         [35]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Both parties have since reconstituted. They share common ideals, but one represents the middle class and the latter the interests of the Salvadoran military.
      </p>
      <p>
       PDC leader
       <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Napole%C3%B3n_Duarte" title="José Napoleón Duarte">
        José Napoleón Duarte
       </a>
       was the mayor of
       <a href="/wiki/San_Salvador" title="San Salvador">
        San Salvador
       </a>
       from 1964 to 1970, winning three elections during the regime of PCN President
       <a href="/wiki/Julio_Adalberto_Rivera_Carballo" title="Julio Adalberto Rivera Carballo">
        Julio Adalberto Rivera Carballo
       </a>
       , who allowed free elections for mayors and the National Assembly. Duarte later ran for president with a political grouping called the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/National_Opposition_Union" title="National Opposition Union">
        National Opposition Union
       </a>
       (UNO) but was defeated in the 1972 presidential elections. He lost to the ex-Minister of Interior, Col.
       <a href="/wiki/Arturo_Armando_Molina" title="Arturo Armando Molina">
        Arturo Armando Molina
       </a>
       , in an election that was widely viewed as fraudulent; Molina was declared the winner even though Duarte was said to have received a majority of the votes. Duarte, at some army officers' request, supported a revolt to protest the election fraud, but was captured, tortured and later exiled. Duarte returned to the country in 1979 to enter politics after working on projects in Venezuela as an engineer.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span id="Salvadoran_Civil_War_.281979.E2.80.931992.29">
       </span>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Salvadoran_Civil_War_(1979–1992)">
        Salvadoran Civil War (1979–1992)
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Further information:
       <a href="/wiki/Salvadoran_Civil_War" title="Salvadoran Civil War">
        Salvadoran Civil War
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       In October 1979, a
       <a href="/wiki/Coup_d%27%C3%A9tat" title="Coup d'état">
        coup d'état
       </a>
       brought the
       <a href="/wiki/Revolutionary_Government_Junta_of_El_Salvador" title="Revolutionary Government Junta of El Salvador">
        Revolutionary Government Junta of El Salvador
       </a>
       to power. It nationalized many private companies and took over much privately owned land. The purpose of this new junta was to stop the revolutionary movement already underway in response to Duarte's stolen election. Nevertheless, the oligarchy opposed
       <a href="/wiki/Agrarian_reform" title="Agrarian reform">
        agrarian reform
       </a>
       , and a junta formed with young liberal elements from the army such as
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/El_Salvador_Civil_War" title="El Salvador Civil War">
        Gen. Majano and Gen. Gutierrez
       </a>
       ,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36">
        <a href="#cite_note-36">
         [36]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37">
        <a href="#cite_note-37">
         [37]
        </a>
       </sup>
       as well as with progressives such as
       <a href="/wiki/Guillermo_Ungo" title="Guillermo Ungo">
        Guillermo Ungo
       </a>
       and Alvarez.
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Masakro-%C4%89e-Suchitoto-Salvadoro.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="546" data-file-width="818" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/Masakro-%C4%89e-Suchitoto-Salvadoro.jpg/220px-Masakro-%C4%89e-Suchitoto-Salvadoro.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/Masakro-%C4%89e-Suchitoto-Salvadoro.jpg/330px-Masakro-%C4%89e-Suchitoto-Salvadoro.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/Masakro-%C4%89e-Suchitoto-Salvadoro.jpg/440px-Masakro-%C4%89e-Suchitoto-Salvadoro.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Masakro-%C4%89e-Suchitoto-Salvadoro.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         A billboard serving as a reminder of one of many
         <a href="/wiki/List_of_massacres_in_El_Salvador" title="List of massacres in El Salvador">
          massacres
         </a>
         that occurred during the civil war.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Pressure from the oligarchy soon dissolved the junta because of its inability to control the army in its repression of the people fighting for unionization rights, agrarian reform, better wages, accessible health care and freedom of expression. In the meantime, the guerrilla movement was spreading to all sectors of Salvadoran society. Middle and high school students were organized in MERS (Movimiento Estudiantil Revolucionario de Secundaria, Revolutionary Movement of Secondary Students); college students were involved with AGEUS (Asociacion de Estudiantes Universitarios Salvadorenos; Association of Salvadoran College Students); and workers were organized in BPR (Bloque Popular Revolucionario, Popular Revolutionary Block). In October 1980, several other major guerrilla groups of the Salvadoran left had formed the
       <a href="/wiki/Farabundo_Mart%C3%AD_National_Liberation_Front" title="Farabundo Martí National Liberation Front">
        Farabundo Martí National Liberation Front
       </a>
       , or FMLN. By the end of the 1970s, death squads were killing about 10 people each day, and the FMLN had 6,000 – 8,000 active guerrillas and hundreds of thousands of part-time militia, supporters, and sympathizers.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38">
        <a href="#cite_note-38">
         [38]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:292px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:ERP_combatants_Perqu%C3%ADn_1990_24.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="500" data-file-width="736" height="197" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/ERP_combatants_Perqu%C3%ADn_1990_24.jpg/290px-ERP_combatants_Perqu%C3%ADn_1990_24.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/ERP_combatants_Perqu%C3%ADn_1990_24.jpg/435px-ERP_combatants_Perqu%C3%ADn_1990_24.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/ERP_combatants_Perqu%C3%ADn_1990_24.jpg/580px-ERP_combatants_Perqu%C3%ADn_1990_24.jpg 2x" width="290"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:ERP_combatants_Perqu%C3%ADn_1990_24.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Farabundo_Mart%C3%AD_National_Liberation_Front" title="Farabundo Martí National Liberation Front">
          ERP
         </a>
         combatants in
         <a href="/wiki/Perqu%C3%ADn" title="Perquín">
          Perquín
         </a>
         , 1990.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The U.S. supported and financed the creation of a second junta to change the political environment and stop the spread of a leftist insurrection. Napoleón Duarte was recalled from his exile in Venezuela to head this new junta. However, a revolution was already underway and his new role as head of the junta was seen by the general population as opportunistic. He was unable to influence the outcome of the insurrection.
       <a href="/wiki/%C3%93scar_Romero" title="Óscar Romero">
        Monsignor Romero
       </a>
       , Archbishop of San Salvador, denounced injustices and massacres committed against civilians by government forces. He was considered "the voice of the voiceless", but he was assassinated by a
       <a href="/wiki/Death_squad" title="Death squad">
        death squad
       </a>
       while saying Mass on 24 March 1980.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39">
        <a href="#cite_note-39">
         [39]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Some consider this to be the beginning of the full
       <a href="/wiki/Salvadoran_Civil_War" title="Salvadoran Civil War">
        Salvadoran Civil War
       </a>
       , which lasted from 1980 to 1992. An unknown number of people "disappeared" during the conflict, and the UN reports that more than 75,000 were killed.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40">
        <a href="#cite_note-40">
         [40]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Salvadoran_Army" title="Salvadoran Army">
        Salvadoran Army
       </a>
       's US-trained
       <a href="/wiki/Atlacatl_Battalion" title="Atlacatl Battalion">
        Atlacatl Battalion
       </a>
       was responsible for the
       <a href="/wiki/El_Mozote_massacre" title="El Mozote massacre">
        El Mozote massacre
       </a>
       where more than 800 civilians were murdered, over half of them children, the
       <a href="/wiki/El_Calabozo_massacre" title="El Calabozo massacre">
        El Calabozo massacre
       </a>
       , and the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Murder_of_UCA_scholars" title="Murder of UCA scholars">
        murder of UCA scholars
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41">
        <a href="#cite_note-41">
         [41]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Radio_Venceremos_Reconstruction.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1200" data-file-width="1600" height="225" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Radio_Venceremos_Reconstruction.jpg/300px-Radio_Venceremos_Reconstruction.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Radio_Venceremos_Reconstruction.jpg/450px-Radio_Venceremos_Reconstruction.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Radio_Venceremos_Reconstruction.jpg/600px-Radio_Venceremos_Reconstruction.jpg 2x" width="300"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Radio_Venceremos_Reconstruction.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         A reconstruction of
         <a href="/wiki/Radio_Venceremos" title="Radio Venceremos">
          Radio Venceremos
         </a>
         , at the
         <a href="/wiki/Museo_de_la_Palabra_y_la_Imagen" title="Museo de la Palabra y la Imagen">
          Museo de la Palabra y la Imagen
         </a>
         , San Salvador.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       On January 16, 1992, the government of El Salvador, represented by president
       <a href="/wiki/Alfredo_Cristiani" title="Alfredo Cristiani">
        Alfredo Cristiani
       </a>
       , and the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/FMLN" title="FMLN">
        FMLN
       </a>
       , represented by the commanders of the five guerrilla groups –
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Shafik_Handal" title="Shafik Handal">
        Shafik Handal
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Joaqu%C3%ADn_Villalobos" title="Joaquín Villalobos">
        Joaquín Villalobos
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Salvador_S%C3%A1nchez_Cer%C3%A9n" title="Salvador Sánchez Cerén">
        Salvador Sánchez Cerén
       </a>
       , Francisco Jovel and
       <a href="/wiki/Ferm%C3%A1n_Cienfuegos" title="Fermán Cienfuegos">
        Eduardo Sancho
       </a>
       , all signed peace agreements brokered by the United Nations ending the 12-year civil war. This event, held at
       <a href="/wiki/Chapultepec_Castle" title="Chapultepec Castle">
        Chapultepec Castle
       </a>
       in Mexico, was attended by U.N. dignitaries and other representatives of the international community. After signing the armistice, the president stood up and shook hands with all the now ex-guerrilla commanders, an action which was widely admired.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span id="Post-war_.281992.E2.80.93present.29">
       </span>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Post-war_(1992–present)">
        Post-war (1992–present)
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       The so-called
       <a href="/wiki/Chapultepec_Peace_Accords" title="Chapultepec Peace Accords">
        Chapultepec Peace Accords
       </a>
       mandated reductions in the size of the army, and the dissolution of the National Police, the Treasury Police, the National Guard and the Civilian Defense, a paramilitary group. A new Civil Police was to be organized. Judicial immunity for crimes committed by the armed forces ended; the government agreed to submit to the recommendations of a
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Commission_on_the_Truth_for_El_Salvador" title="Commission on the Truth for El Salvador">
        Commission on the Truth for El Salvador
       </a>
       <i>
        (Comisión de la Verdad Para El Salvador)
       </i>
       , which would "investigate serious acts of violence occurring since 1980, and the nature and effects of the violence, and...recommend methods of promoting national reconciliation." In 1993 the Commission delivered its findings reporting human rights violations on both sides of the conflict.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42">
        <a href="#cite_note-42">
         [42]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Five days later the El Salvadoran legislature passed an amnesty law for all acts of violence during the period.
      </p>
      <p>
       From 1989 until 2004, Salvadorans favored the
       <a href="/wiki/Nationalist_Republican_Alliance" title="Nationalist Republican Alliance">
        Nationalist Republican Alliance
       </a>
       (ARENA) party, voting in ARENA presidents in every election (
       <a href="/wiki/Alfredo_Cristiani" title="Alfredo Cristiani">
        Alfredo Cristiani
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Armando_Calder%C3%B3n_Sol" title="Armando Calderón Sol">
        Armando Calderón Sol
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Francisco_Flores_P%C3%A9rez" title="Francisco Flores Pérez">
        Francisco Flores Pérez
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Antonio_Saca" title="Antonio Saca">
        Antonio Saca
       </a>
       ) until 2009, when
       <a href="/wiki/Mauricio_Funes" title="Mauricio Funes">
        Mauricio Funes
       </a>
       was elected president from the
       <a href="/wiki/Farabundo_Mart%C3%AD_National_Liberation_Front" title="Farabundo Martí National Liberation Front">
        Farabundo Martí National Liberation Front
       </a>
       (FMLN) party.
      </p>
      <p>
       Economic reforms since the early 1990s brought major benefits in terms of improved social conditions, diversification of the export sector, and access to international financial markets at investment grade level. Crime remains a major problem for the investment climate.
      </p>
      <p>
       This
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify">
          <span title="The text near this tag may need clarification or removal of jargon. (July 2016)">
           clarification needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       all ended in 2001, and support for ARENA weakened. Internal turmoil in ARENA weakened the party also, while the FMLN united and broadened its support.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43">
        <a href="#cite_note-43">
         [43]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The unsuccessful attempts of the left-wing party to win presidential elections led to its selection of a journalist rather than a former guerrilla leader as a candidate. On March 15, 2009,
       <a href="/wiki/Mauricio_Funes" title="Mauricio Funes">
        Mauricio Funes
       </a>
       , a television figure, became the first president from the
       <a href="/wiki/Farabundo_Mart%C3%AD_National_Liberation_Front" title="Farabundo Martí National Liberation Front">
        FMLN
       </a>
       party. He was inaugurated on June 1, 2009. One focus of the Funes government has been revealing the alleged corruption from the past government.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44">
        <a href="#cite_note-44">
         [44]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       ARENA formally expelled Saca from the party in December 2009. With 12 loyalists in the National Assembly, Saca established his own party, GANA (Gran Alianza por la Unidad Nacional or
       <a href="/wiki/Grand_Alliance_for_National_Unity" title="Grand Alliance for National Unity">
        Grand Alliance for National Unity
       </a>
       ), and entered into a tactical legislative alliance with the FMLN.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45">
        <a href="#cite_note-45">
         [45]
        </a>
       </sup>
       After three years in office, with Saca's GANA party providing the FMLN with a legislative majority, Funes had not taken action to either investigate or to bring corrupt former officials to justice.
      </p>
      <p>
       Early in the new millennium, El Salvador's government created the Ministerio de Medio Ambiente y Recursos Naturales – the Ministry of Environment and Natural Resources (MARN) and began promoting the integration of climate change into national policy. This move was in response to the increase in extreme weather events affecting the country. Initially MARN aimed to fulfil the country’s obligations following its ratification of the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/UNFCCC" title="UNFCCC">
        UNFCCC
       </a>
       and the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kyoto_protocol" title="Kyoto protocol">
        Kyoto protocol
       </a>
       However, since Hurricane Ida in 2009, the government’s stance has shifted towards integrating risk reduction into all areas of policy, including financial.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cdkn.org_46-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-cdkn.org-46">
         [46]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In a specific effort to increase the resilience of its economy and people to climate-related events, El Salvador commissioned a project in 2011 to develop and implement a National Policy and Strategy for Climate Change, which culminated with the launch of the National Environmental Policy in June 2012 and the National Environmental Strategy in June 2013, both incorporating climate change goals. This work was undertaken with support from the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Climate_%26_Development_Knowledge_Network" title="Climate &amp; Development Knowledge Network">
        Climate &amp; Development Knowledge Network
       </a>
       . The government is now preparing action plans for putting the strategy into practice.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cdkn.org_46-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-cdkn.org-46">
         [46]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">
        Geography
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_El_Salvador" title="Geography of El Salvador">
        Geography of El Salvador
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="center">
       <div class="thumb tnone">
        <div class="thumbinner" style="width:802px;">
         <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Cerro_verde.jpg">
          <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="450" data-file-width="2048" height="176" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/Cerro_verde.jpg/800px-Cerro_verde.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/Cerro_verde.jpg/1200px-Cerro_verde.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/Cerro_verde.jpg/1600px-Cerro_verde.jpg 2x" width="800"/>
         </a>
         <div class="thumbcaption">
          <div class="magnify">
           <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Cerro_verde.jpg" title="Enlarge">
           </a>
          </div>
          Panoramic of
          <a href="/wiki/Coatepeque_Caldera" title="Coatepeque Caldera">
           Coatepeque Caldera
          </a>
          , Cerro Verde and
          <a href="/wiki/Izalco_(volcano)" title="Izalco (volcano)">
           Izalco (volcano)
          </a>
         </div>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Un-el-salvador.png">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1926" data-file-width="2590" height="126" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/Un-el-salvador.png/170px-Un-el-salvador.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/Un-el-salvador.png/255px-Un-el-salvador.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/Un-el-salvador.png/340px-Un-el-salvador.png 2x" width="170"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Un-el-salvador.png" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         A map of El Salvador
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       El Salvador lies in the isthmus of Central America between latitudes
       <a href="/wiki/13th_parallel_north" title="13th parallel north">
        13°
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/15th_parallel_north" title="15th parallel north">
        15°N
       </a>
       , and longitudes
       <a href="/wiki/87th_meridian_west" title="87th meridian west">
        87°
       </a>
       and
