       <a href="/wiki/91st_meridian_west" title="91st meridian west">
        91°W
       </a>
       . It stretches 270 km (168 mi) from west-northwest to east-southeast and 142 km (88 mi) north to south, with a total area of 21,041 km
       <sup>
        2
       </sup>
       (8,124 sq mi). As the smallest country in continental America, El Salvador is affectionately called
       <i>
        Pulgarcito de America
       </i>
       (the "
       <a href="/wiki/Tom_Thumb" title="Tom Thumb">
        Tom Thumb
       </a>
       of the Americas"). The highest point in El Salvador is
       <a href="/wiki/Cerro_El_Pital" title="Cerro El Pital">
        Cerro El Pital
       </a>
       , at 2,730 metres (8,957 ft), on the border with
       <a href="/wiki/Honduras" title="Honduras">
        Honduras
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       El Salvador has a long history of
       <a href="/wiki/List_of_earthquakes_in_El_Salvador" title="List of earthquakes in El Salvador">
        destructive earthquakes
       </a>
       and volcanic eruptions. The capital San Salvador was destroyed in 1756 and 1854, and it suffered heavy damage in the 1919, 1982, and 1986 tremors. El Salvador has over twenty volcanoes, two of them, San Miguel and
       <a href="/wiki/Izalco_(volcano)" title="Izalco (volcano)">
        Izalco
       </a>
       , active in recent years. From the early 19th century to the mid-1950s, Izalco erupted with a regularity that earned it the name "Lighthouse of the Pacific." Its brilliant flares were clearly visible for great distances at sea, and at night its glowing lava turned it into a brilliant luminous cone.
      </p>
      <p>
       El Salvador has over 300 rivers, the most important of which is the Rio Lempa. Originating in Guatemala, the Rio Lempa cuts across the northern range of mountains, flows along much of the central plateau, and cuts through the southern volcanic range to empty into the Pacific. It is El Salvador's only navigable river. It and its tributaries drain about half of the country's area. Other rivers are generally short and drain the Pacific lowlands or flow from the central plateau through gaps in the southern mountain range to the Pacific. These include the
       <a href="/wiki/Goascor%C3%A1n_River" title="Goascorán River">
        Goascorán
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Jiboa_River" title="Jiboa River">
        Jiboa
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Torola_River" title="Torola River">
        Torola
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Paz_River" title="Paz River">
        Paz
       </a>
       and the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/R%C3%ADo_Grande_de_San_Miguel" title="Río Grande de San Miguel">
        Río Grande de San Miguel
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       There are several lakes enclosed by volcanic craters in El Salvador, the most important of which are
       <a href="/wiki/Lake_Ilopango" title="Lake Ilopango">
        Lake Ilopango
       </a>
       (70 km²) and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lake_Coatepeque" title="Lake Coatepeque">
        Lake Coatepeque
       </a>
       (26 km²).
       <a href="/wiki/Lake_G%C3%BCija" title="Lake Güija">
        Lake Güija
       </a>
       is El Salvador's largest natural lake (44 km²). Several artificial lakes were created by the damming of the Lempa, the largest of which is
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cerr%C3%B3n_Grande_Hydroelectric_Dam" title="Cerrón Grande Hydroelectric Dam">
        Embalse Cerrón Grande
       </a>
       (135 km²). There are a total 320 km
       <sup>
        2
       </sup>
       (123.6 sq mi) of water within El Salvador's borders.
      </p>
      <p>
       El Salvador shares borders with Guatemala and Honduras, the total national boundary length is 546 km (339 mi): 126 miles (203 km) with Guatemala and 343 km (213 mi) with Honduras. It is the only Central American country that has no Caribbean coastline. The coastline on the Pacific is 307 km (191 mi) long.
      </p>
      <p>
       Two parallel mountain ranges cross El Salvador to the west with a central plateau between them and a narrow coastal plain hugging the Pacific. These physical features divide the country into two physiographic regions. The mountain ranges and central
       <a href="/wiki/Plateau" title="Plateau">
        plateau
       </a>
       , covering 85% of the land, comprise the interior highlands. The remaining coastal plains are referred to as the Pacific lowlands.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">
        Climate
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Climate_of_El_Salvador" title="Climate of El Salvador">
        Climate of El Salvador
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:El_Salvador_Topography.png">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1797" data-file-width="1963" height="201" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/El_Salvador_Topography.png/220px-El_Salvador_Topography.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/El_Salvador_Topography.png/330px-El_Salvador_Topography.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/El_Salvador_Topography.png/440px-El_Salvador_Topography.png 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:El_Salvador_Topography.png" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         El Salvador's topography.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       El Salvador has a
       <a href="/wiki/Tropical_climate" title="Tropical climate">
        Tropical climate
       </a>
       with pronounced wet and dry seasons. Temperatures vary primarily with elevation and show little seasonal change. The Pacific lowlands are uniformly hot; the central plateau and mountain areas are more moderate. The rainy season extends from May to October; this time of year is referred to as
       <i>
        invierno
       </i>
       or winter. Almost all the annual rainfall occurs during this period; yearly totals, particularly on southern-facing mountain slopes, can be as high as 2170 mm.
      </p>
      <p>
       The best time to visit El Salvador would be at the beginning or end of the dry season. Protected areas and the central plateau receive less, although still significant, amounts. Rainfall during this season generally comes from low pressure systems formed over the Pacific and usually falls in heavy afternoon thunderstorms.
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hurricane" title="Hurricane">
        Hurricanes
       </a>
       occasionally form in the Pacific with the notable exception of
       <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Mitch" title="Hurricane Mitch">
        Hurricane Mitch
       </a>
       , which formed in the Atlantic and crossed Central America.
      </p>
      <p>
       From November through April, the northeast
       <a href="/wiki/Trade_winds" title="Trade winds">
        trade winds
       </a>
       control weather patterns; this time of year is referred to as
       <i>
        verano
       </i>
       , or summer. During these months, air flowing from the Caribbean has lost most of its precipitation while passing over the mountains in
       <a href="/wiki/Honduras" title="Honduras">
        Honduras
       </a>
       . By the time this air reaches El Salvador, it is dry, hot, and hazy, and the country experiences hot weather, excluding the northern higher mountain ranges, where temperatures will be cool. In the extreme northeastern part of the country near
       <a href="/wiki/Cerro_El_Pital" title="Cerro El Pital">
        Cerro El Pital
       </a>
       , snow is known to fall during summer as well as during winter due to the high elevations (it is the coldest part of the country).
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Natural_disasters">
        Natural disasters
       </span>
      </h3>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Extreme_weather_events">
        Extreme weather events
       </span>
      </h4>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Salcoatit%C3%A1n,_El_Salvador_-_panoramio_(9).jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1200" data-file-width="1600" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/Salcoatit%C3%A1n%2C_El_Salvador_-_panoramio_%289%29.jpg/220px-Salcoatit%C3%A1n%2C_El_Salvador_-_panoramio_%289%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/Salcoatit%C3%A1n%2C_El_Salvador_-_panoramio_%289%29.jpg/330px-Salcoatit%C3%A1n%2C_El_Salvador_-_panoramio_%289%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/Salcoatit%C3%A1n%2C_El_Salvador_-_panoramio_%289%29.jpg/440px-Salcoatit%C3%A1n%2C_El_Salvador_-_panoramio_%289%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Salcoatit%C3%A1n,_El_Salvador_-_panoramio_(9).jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Volcanic range,
         <a href="/wiki/Cordillera_de_Apaneca" title="Cordillera de Apaneca">
          Cordillera de Apaneca
         </a>
         , view from
         <a href="/wiki/Salcoatit%C3%A1n" title="Salcoatitán">
          Salcoatitán
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       El Salvador's position on the Pacific Ocean also makes it subject to severe weather conditions, including heavy rainstorms and severe
       <a href="/wiki/Drought" title="Drought">
        droughts
       </a>
       , both of which may be made more extreme by the
       <a href="/wiki/El_Ni%C3%B1o" title="El Niño">
        El Niño
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/La_Ni%C3%B1a" title="La Niña">
        La Niña
       </a>
       effects. Severe deforestation and soil erosion have made the landscape vulnerable to landslides and forest fires. These characteristics, coupled with severe fiscal constraints, make the nation highly susceptible to the impacts of extreme weather events.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47">
        <a href="#cite_note-47">
         [47]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In the summer of 2001 a severe drought destroyed 80% of El Salvador's crops, causing
       <a href="/wiki/Famine" title="Famine">
        famine
       </a>
       in the countryside.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48">
        <a href="#cite_note-48">
         [48]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49">
        <a href="#cite_note-49">
         [49]
        </a>
       </sup>
       On October 4, 2005, severe rains resulted in dangerous flooding and
       <a href="/wiki/Landslide" title="Landslide">
        landslides
       </a>
       , which caused a minimum of fifty deaths.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tdfiyp_50-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-tdfiyp-50">
         [50]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In 2010, losses to agriculture from flooding exceeded USD100 million, while those resulting from drought were USD38 million.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51">
        <a href="#cite_note-51">
         [51]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       El Salvador's location in Central America also makes it vulnerable to severe storms and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hurricane" title="Hurricane">
        hurricanes
       </a>
       coming off the Caribbean. Since the 1990s, there has been an increase in the frequency and duration of storms, as well as a marked change in the pattern of their occurrence. Hurricanes used to strike El Salvador infrequently, only came from the Atlantic and were limited to the months of September and October. However, since the mid 1990s, such storms have occurred more frequently, originated in both the Atlantic and Pacific, and have struck in six different months of the year.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cdkn.org_46-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-cdkn.org-46">
         [46]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Earthquakes_and_volcanic_activity">
        Earthquakes and volcanic activity
       </span>
      </h4>
      <p>
       El Salvador lies along the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pacific_Ring_of_Fire" title="Pacific Ring of Fire">
        Pacific Ring of Fire
       </a>
       , and is thus subject to significant
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tectonic_plate" title="Tectonic plate">
        tectonic
       </a>
       activity, including frequent
       <a href="/wiki/Earthquake" title="Earthquake">
        earthquakes
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Volcano" title="Volcano">
        volcanic
       </a>
       activity. Recent examples include the earthquake on January 13, 2001 that measured 7.7 on the
       <a href="/wiki/Richter_magnitude_scale" title="Richter magnitude scale">
        Richter magnitude scale
       </a>
       and caused a
       <a href="/wiki/Landslide" title="Landslide">
        landslide
       </a>
       that killed more than 800 people;
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tdfiyp_50-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-tdfiyp-50">
         [50]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and another earthquake only a month later, on February 13, 2001, that killed 255 people and damaged about 20% of the nation's housing. Luckily, many families were able to find safety from the landslides caused by the earthquake.
      </p>
      <p>
       The San Salvador area has been hit by earthquakes in 1576, 1659, 1798, 1839, 1854, 1873, 1880, 1917, 1919, 1965, 1986, 2001 and 2005.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52">
        <a href="#cite_note-52">
         [52]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Moment_magnitude_scale" title="Moment magnitude scale">
        5.7 M
        <sub>
         w
        </sub>
       </a>
       -earthquake of 1986 resulted in 1,500 deaths, 10,000 injuries, and 100,000 people left homeless.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53">
        <a href="#cite_note-53">
         [53]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54">
        <a href="#cite_note-54">
         [54]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       El Salvador's most recent destructive volcanic eruption took place on October 1, 2005, when the
       <a href="/wiki/Santa_Ana_Volcano" title="Santa Ana Volcano">
        Santa Ana Volcano
       </a>
       spewed a cloud of ash, hot mud and rocks that fell on nearby villages and caused two deaths. The most severe volcanic eruption in this area occurred in the 5th century AD when the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ilopango_(volcano)" title="Ilopango (volcano)">
        Ilopango
       </a>
       volcano erupted with a
       <a href="/wiki/Volcanic_Explosivity_Index" title="Volcanic Explosivity Index">
        VEI
       </a>
       strength of 6, producing widespread
       <a href="/wiki/Pyroclastic_flow" title="Pyroclastic flow">
        pyroclastic flows
       </a>
       and devastating
       <a href="/wiki/Maya_civilization" title="Maya civilization">
        Mayan cities
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55">
        <a href="#cite_note-55">
         [55]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Santa_Ana_Volcano" title="Santa Ana Volcano">
        Santa Ana Volcano
       </a>
       in El Salvador is active;
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56">
        <a href="#cite_note-56">
         [56]
        </a>
       </sup>
       the most recent eruptions were in 1904 and 2005.
       <a href="/wiki/Coatepeque_Caldera" title="Coatepeque Caldera">
        Lago de Coatepeque
       </a>
       (one of El Salvador's lakes) was created by water filling the
       <a href="/wiki/Caldera" title="Caldera">
        caldera
       </a>
       that formed after a massive eruption.
      </p>
      <p>
       The British
       <a href="/wiki/Imperial_College_London" title="Imperial College London">
        Imperial College's
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/El_Salvador_Project" title="El Salvador Project">
        El Salvador Project
       </a>
       aims to build earthquake-proof buildings in remote areas of the country.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Biodiversity_and_endangered_species">
        Biodiversity and endangered species
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Motmot1.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="400" data-file-width="255" height="345" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/Motmot1.jpg/220px-Motmot1.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/9/9e/Motmot1.jpg 1.5x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Motmot1.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         The torogoz is El Salvador's national bird.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       There are eight species of sea turtles in the world; six of them nest on the coasts of Central America, and four make their home on the Salvadoran coast: the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Leatherback_turtle" title="Leatherback turtle">
        leatherback turtle
       </a>
       (
       <i>
        Dermochelys coriacea
       </i>
       ), the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hawksbill_turtle" title="Hawksbill turtle">
        hawksbill
       </a>
       (
       <i>
        Eretmochelys imbricata
       </i>
       ), the green sea turtle (
       <i>
        Chelonia agasizzii
       </i>
       ) and the
       <a href="/wiki/Olive_ridley_sea_turtle" title="Olive ridley sea turtle">
        olive ridley
       </a>
       (
       <i>
        Lepidochelys olivacea
       </i>
       ). Of these four species, the most common is the olive ridley turtle, followed by the green sea turtle. The other two species, hawksbill and leatherback, are much more difficult to find as they are critically endangered, while the olive ridley and green sea turtle are in danger of extinction.
      </p>
      <p>
       Recent conservation efforts provide hope for the future of the country's biological diversity. In 1997, the government established the Ministry of the Environment and Natural Resources. A general environmental framework law was approved by the National Assembly in 1999. Specific legislation to protect wildlife is still pending.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers#Chronological_items" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers">
          <span title="The time period mentioned near this tag is ambiguous. (July 2016)">
           when?
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       In addition, a number of non-governmental organizations are doing important work to safeguard some of the country's most important forested areas. Foremost among these is SalvaNatura, which manages El Impossible, the country's largest national park under an agreement with El Salvador's environmental authorities.
      </p>
      <p>
       Despite these efforts, much remains to be done.
      </p>
      <p>
       It is estimated that there are 500 species of birds, 1,000 species of butterflies, 400 species of orchids, 800 species of trees, and 800 species of marine fish in El Salvador.
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Government_and_politics">
        Government and politics
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_El_Salvador" title="Politics of El Salvador">
        Politics of El Salvador
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       The 1983 Constitution is the highest legal authority in the country. El Salvador has a democratic and representative government, whose three bodies are:
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Sesion_Solemne_de_Legislatura_2015-2018_(17866066655).jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3456" data-file-width="5184" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/Sesion_Solemne_de_Legislatura_2015-2018_%2817866066655%29.jpg/220px-Sesion_Solemne_de_Legislatura_2015-2018_%2817866066655%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/Sesion_Solemne_de_Legislatura_2015-2018_%2817866066655%29.jpg/330px-Sesion_Solemne_de_Legislatura_2015-2018_%2817866066655%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/Sesion_Solemne_de_Legislatura_2015-2018_%2817866066655%29.jpg/440px-Sesion_Solemne_de_Legislatura_2015-2018_%2817866066655%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Sesion_Solemne_de_Legislatura_2015-2018_(17866066655).jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Salvadoran cadets in the Legislative Assembly of El Salvador
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <ol>
       <li>
        The Executive Branch, headed by the President of the Republic, who is elected by direct vote and remains in office for five years. He can be elected to only one term. The president has a Cabinet of Ministers whom he appoints, and is also the Commander-in-Chief of the Armed Forces.
       </li>
       <li>
        The Legislative Branch, called El Salvador's Legislative Assembly (unicameral), consisting of 84 deputies.
       </li>
       <li>
        The Judiciary, headed by the Supreme Court, which is composed of 15 judges, one of them being elected as President of the Judiciary.
       </li>
       <li class="mw-empty-elt">
       </li>
      </ol>
      <p>
       After the Civil War, the Chapultepec Peace Accords (1992) created the new National Civil Police, the Attorney for the Defense of Human Rights and the Supreme Electoral Tribunal. The Peace Accords re-imagined the
       <i>
        Frente Farabundo Martí para la Liberación Nacional
       </i>
       (FMLN) as a political party and redefined the role of the army to be for the defense of the sovereignty and territorial integrity. The Accords also removed some security forces who were in command of the army, such as the National Guard, Treasury Police and special battalions that were formed to fight against the insurgency of the 1980s.
      </p>
      <p>
       The political framework of El Salvador is a
       <a href="/wiki/Presidential_system" title="Presidential system">
        presidential
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Representative_democracy" title="Representative democracy">
        representative democratic
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Republic" title="Republic">
        republic
       </a>
       with a multiform, multi-party system. The
       <a href="/wiki/President_of_El_Salvador" title="President of El Salvador">
        President
       </a>
       , currently
       <a href="/wiki/Salvador_S%C3%A1nchez_Cer%C3%A9n" title="Salvador Sánchez Cerén">
        Salvador Sánchez Cerén
       </a>
       , is both
       <a href="/wiki/Head_of_state" title="Head of state">
        head of state
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Head_of_government" title="Head of government">
        head of government
       </a>
       .
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Executive_power" title="Executive power">
        Executive power
       </a>
       is exercised by the government.
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Legislative_power" title="Legislative power">
        Legislative power
       </a>
       is vested in both the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Forms_of_government" title="Forms of government">
        government
       </a>
       and the
       <a href="/wiki/Legislative_Assembly_of_El_Salvador" title="Legislative Assembly of El Salvador">
        Legislative Assembly
       </a>
       . The country also has an independent
       <a href="/wiki/Judiciary" title="Judiciary">
        Judiciary
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Court_of_El_Salvador" title="Supreme Court of El Salvador">
        Supreme Court
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Political_culture">
        Political culture
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Further information:
       <a href="/wiki/List_of_political_parties_in_El_Salvador" title="List of political parties in El Salvador">
        List of political parties in El Salvador
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Salvador_Sanchez_Ceren.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1096" data-file-width="834" height="263" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/Salvador_Sanchez_Ceren.jpg/200px-Salvador_Sanchez_Ceren.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/Salvador_Sanchez_Ceren.jpg/300px-Salvador_Sanchez_Ceren.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/Salvador_Sanchez_Ceren.jpg/400px-Salvador_Sanchez_Ceren.jpg 2x" width="200"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Salvador_Sanchez_Ceren.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Salvador_S%C3%A1nchez_Cer%C3%A9n" title="Salvador Sánchez Cerén">
          Salvador Sánchez Cerén
         </a>
         is El Salvador's president.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       El Salvador has a
       <a href="/wiki/Multi-party_system" title="Multi-party system">
        multi-party system
       </a>
       . Two
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Political_parties" title="Political parties">
        political parties
       </a>
       , the
       <a href="/wiki/Nationalist_Republican_Alliance" title="Nationalist Republican Alliance">
        Nationalist Republican Alliance
       </a>
       (ARENA) and the
       <a href="/wiki/Farabundo_Mart%C3%AD_National_Liberation_Front" title="Farabundo Martí National Liberation Front">
        Farabundo Martí National Liberation Front
       </a>
       (FMLN) have tended to dominate elections.
       <a href="/wiki/Nationalist_Republican_Alliance" title="Nationalist Republican Alliance">
        ARENA
       </a>
       candidates won four consecutive presidential elections until the election of
       <a href="/wiki/Mauricio_Funes" title="Mauricio Funes">
        Mauricio Funes
       </a>
       of the FMLN in March 2009. The FMLN Party is Leftist in ideology, and is split between the dominant
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Marxist-Leninist" title="Marxist-Leninist">
        Marxist-Leninist
       </a>
       faction in the legislature, and the
       <a href="/wiki/Social_liberalism" title="Social liberalism">
        social liberal
       </a>
       wing led by President Funes.
      </p>
      <p>
       Geographically,
       <a href="/wiki/Departments_of_El_Salvador" title="Departments of El Salvador">
        the departments
       </a>
       of the Central region, especially the capital and the coastal regions, known as departamentos rojos, or red departments, are relatively Leftist. The departamentos azules, or blue departments in the east, western and highland regions are relatively conservative. The winner of the
       <a href="/wiki/Salvadoran_presidential_election,_2014" title="Salvadoran presidential election, 2014">
        2014 presidential election
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Salvador_S%C3%A1nchez_Cer%C3%A9n" title="Salvador Sánchez Cerén">
        Salvador Sánchez Cerén
       </a>
       belongs to the FMLN party. In the 2015 elections for mayors and members of the National Assembly, ARENA appeared to be the winner with tight control of the National Assembly.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Foreign_relations">
        Foreign relations
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Further information:
       <a href="/wiki/Foreign_relations_of_El_Salvador" title="Foreign relations of El Salvador">
        Foreign relations of El Salvador
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       In November, 1950 El Salvador helped the newly empowered
       <a href="/wiki/14th_Dalai_Lama" title="14th Dalai Lama">
        14th Dalai Lama
       </a>
       by supporting his
       <a href="/wiki/Tibet" title="Tibet">
        Tibetan
       </a>
       Government cabinet minister's
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Telegram" title="Telegram">
        telegram
       </a>
       requesting an appeal before the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/General_Assembly_of_the_United_Nations" title="General Assembly of the United Nations">
        General Assembly of the United Nations
       </a>
       to stop the Communist
       <a href="/wiki/China" title="China">
        China
       </a>
       's
       <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Liberation_Army" title="People's Liberation Army">
        People's Liberation Army
       </a>
       's invasion of Tibet. "Only the tiny country of El Salvador agreed to sponsor Tibet's plea."
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_57-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-:0-57">
         [57]
        </a>
       </sup>
       "At the UN, no one was willing to stand up beside El Salvador. The other nations had overriding self-interests, which made it impossible for them to support San Salvador's attempt to bring the invasion before the General Assembly."
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_57-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-:0-57">
         [57]
        </a>
       </sup>
       With no other countries in support, "the UN unanimously dropped the Tibetan plea from its agenda."
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_57-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-:0-57">
         [57]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       El Salvador is a member of the
       <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">
        United Nations
       </a>
       and several of its specialized agencies, the
       <a href="/wiki/Organization_of_American_States" title="Organization of American States">
        Organization of American States
       </a>
       (OAS), the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Central_American_Common_Market" title="Central American Common Market">
        Central American Common Market
       </a>
       (CACM), the
       <a href="/wiki/Central_American_Parliament" title="Central American Parliament">
        Central American Parliament
       </a>
       (PARLACEN), and the
       <a href="/wiki/Central_American_Integration_System" title="Central American Integration System">
        Central American Integration System
       </a>
       (SICA). It actively participates in the Central American Security Commission (CASC), which seeks to promote regional arms control.
      </p>
      <p>
       El Salvador also is a member of the
       <a href="/wiki/World_Trade_Organization" title="World Trade Organization">
        World Trade Organization
       </a>
       and is pursuing regional free trade agreements. An active participant in the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Summit_of_the_Americas" title="Summit of the Americas">
        Summit of the Americas
       </a>
       process, El Salvador chairs a
       <a href="/wiki/Working_group" title="Working group">
        working group
       </a>
       on market access under the
       <a href="/wiki/Free_Trade_Area_of_the_Americas" title="Free Trade Area of the Americas">
        Free Trade Area of the Americas
       </a>
       initiative.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Military">
        Military
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Further information:
       <a href="/wiki/Armed_Forces_of_El_Salvador" title="Armed Forces of El Salvador">
        Armed Forces of El Salvador
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       El Salvador has an army, airforce and modest navy. There are around 17,000 personnel in the armed forces in total.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nationmaster_58-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-nationmaster-58">
         [58]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Human_rights">
        Human rights
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Human_rights_in_El_Salvador" title="Human rights in El Salvador">
        Human rights in El Salvador
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       Amnesty International has drawn attention to several arrests of police officers for unlawful police killings. Other current issues to gain Amnesty International's attention in the past 10 years include missing children, failure of law enforcement to properly investigate and prosecute crimes against women, and rendering
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Labor_unions" title="Labor unions">
        organized labor
       </a>
       illegal.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59">
        <a href="#cite_note-59">
         [59]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In El Salvador if a woman miscarries it is frequently assumed she deliberately induced an
       <a href="/wiki/Abortion" title="Abortion">
        abortion
       </a>
       or could have saved the baby. Women who did not know they were pregnant or who could not have prevented a miscarriage face long prison terms.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60">
        <a href="#cite_note-60">
         [60]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61">
        <a href="#cite_note-61">
         [61]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Administrative_divisions">
        Administrative divisions
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Further information:
       <a href="/wiki/Departments_of_El_Salvador" title="Departments of El Salvador">
        Departments of El Salvador
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       El Salvador is
       <a href="/wiki/Departments_of_El_Salvador" title="Departments of El Salvador">
        divided into 14 departments
       </a>
       (
       <i>
        departamentos
       </i>
       ), which in turn are subdivided into 262
       <a href="/wiki/Municipalities_of_El_Salvador" title="Municipalities of El Salvador">
        municipalities
       </a>
       (
       <i>
        municipios
       </i>
       ).
      </p>
      <p>
       Department names and capitals for the 14 Salvadoran Departments:
      </p>

      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">
        Economy
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_El_Salvador" title="Economy of El Salvador">
        Economy of El Salvador
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:402px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:El_Salvador_Export_Treemap.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="861" data-file-width="1101" height="313" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/El_Salvador_Export_Treemap.jpg/400px-El_Salvador_Export_Treemap.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/El_Salvador_Export_Treemap.jpg/600px-El_Salvador_Export_Treemap.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/El_Salvador_Export_Treemap.jpg/800px-El_Salvador_Export_Treemap.jpg 2x" width="400"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:El_Salvador_Export_Treemap.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         A proportional representation of El Salvador's exports
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       El Salvador's economy has been hampered at times by natural disasters such as earthquakes and hurricanes, by government policies that mandate large economic subsidies, and by official corruption. Subsidies became such a problem that in April 2012, the International Monetary Fund suspended a $750 million loan to the central government. President Funes' chief of cabinet, Alex Segovia, acknowledged that the economy was at the "point of collapse."
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62">
        <a href="#cite_note-62">
         [62]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/Antiguo_Cuscatl%C3%A1n" title="Antiguo Cuscatlán">
        Antiguo Cuscatlán
       </a>
       has the highest per capita income of all the cities in the country, and is a center of international investment.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2015)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       GDP in
       <a href="/wiki/Purchasing_power_parity" title="Purchasing power parity">
        purchasing power parity
       </a>
       (PPP) in 2008 was estimated at $25.895 billion USD. The service sector is the largest component of GDP at 64.1%, followed by the industrial sector at 24.7% (2008 est.). Agriculture represents only 11.2% of GDP (2010 est.)
      </p>
      <p>
       The
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gross_Domestic_Product" title="Gross Domestic Product">
        GDP
       </a>
       grew after 1996 at an annual rate that averaged 3.2% real growth. The government committed to
       <a href="/wiki/Free_market" title="Free market">
        free market
       </a>
       initiatives, and the 2007 GDP's real growth rate was 4.7%.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63">
        <a href="#cite_note-63">
         [63]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In December 1999, net international reserves equaled US $1.8 billion or roughly five months of imports. Having this hard currency buffer to work with, the Salvadoran government undertook a monetary integration plan beginning January 1, 2001 by which the U.S. dollar became legal tender alongside the
       <a href="/wiki/Salvadoran_col%C3%B3n" title="Salvadoran colón">
        Salvadoran colón
       </a>
       , and all formal accounting was done in U.S. dollars. Thus, the government has formally limited the implementing of open market monetary policies to influence short-term variables in the economy. As of September 2007, net
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/International_reserve_system" title="International reserve system">
        international reserves
       </a>
       stood at $2.42 billion.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tdfiyp_50-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-tdfiyp-50">
         [50]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64">
        <a href="#cite_note-64">
         [64]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       It has long been a challenge in El Salvador to develop new growth sectors for a more diversified economy. In the past, the country produced gold and silver,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65">
        <a href="#cite_note-65">
         [65]
        </a>
       </sup>
       but recent attempts to reopen the mining sector, which were expected to add hundreds of millions of dollars to the local economy, collapsed after President Saca shut down the operations of
       <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Rim_Mining_Corporation" title="Pacific Rim Mining Corporation">
        Pacific Rim Mining Corporation
       </a>
       . Nevertheless, according to the Central American Institute for Fiscal Studies (Instituto Centroamericano for Estudios Fiscales, by its acronym in Spanish), the contribution of metallic mining was a minuscule 0.3% of the country's GDP between 2010 and 2015.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66">
        <a href="#cite_note-66">
         [66]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Saca's decision although not lacking political motives, had strong support from local residents and grassroots movements in the country. According to
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/NACLA" title="NACLA">
        NACLA
       </a>
       , incoming President Funes later rejected a company's application for a further permit based on the risk of cyanide contamination on one of the country's main rivers.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67">
        <a href="#cite_note-67">
         [67]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       As with other former colonies, El Salvador was considered a mono-export economy (an economy that depended heavily on one type of export) for many years. During colonial times, El Salvador was a thriving exporter of
       <a href="/wiki/Indigo_dye" title="Indigo dye">
        indigo
       </a>
       , but after the invention of synthetic dyes in the 19th century, the newly created modern state turned to
       <a href="/wiki/Coffee" title="Coffee">
        coffee
       </a>
       as the main export.
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Fdpt18102006bmcha43c.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="355" data-file-width="595" height="179" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Fdpt18102006bmcha43c.jpg/300px-Fdpt18102006bmcha43c.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Fdpt18102006bmcha43c.jpg/450px-Fdpt18102006bmcha43c.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/2/2e/Fdpt18102006bmcha43c.jpg 2x" width="300"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Fdpt18102006bmcha43c.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/San_Miguel,_El_Salvador" title="San Miguel, El Salvador">
          San Miguel
         </a>
         is an important economic center of El Salvador and home to the "Carnival of San Miguel", one of the biggest festivals of entertainment and food in Central America.
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Herrera-Sobek2012_68-0">
          <a href="#cite_note-Herrera-Sobek2012-68">
           [68]
          </a>
         </sup>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The government has sought to improve the collection of its current
       <a href="/wiki/Revenue" title="Revenue">
        revenues
       </a>
       , with a focus on indirect taxes. A 10%
       <a href="/wiki/Value-added_tax" title="Value-added tax">
        value-added tax
       </a>
       (IVA in Spanish), implemented in September 1992, was raised to 13% in July 1995.
      </p>
      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/Inflation" title="Inflation">
        Inflation
       </a>
       has been steady and among the lowest in the region. Since 1997 inflation has averaged 3%, with recent years increasing to nearly 5%. As a result of the free trade agreements, from 2000 to 2006, total exports have grown 19% from $2.94 billion to $3.51 billion, and total imports have risen 54% from $4.95 billion to $7.63 billion. This has resulted in a 102% increase in the trade deficit, from $2.01 billion to $4.12 billion.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69">
        <a href="#cite_note-69">
         [69]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:El_Chorreron,_San_Fernando,_El_Salvador.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="581" data-file-width="432" height="296" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/El_Chorreron%2C_San_Fernando%2C_El_Salvador.jpg/220px-El_Chorreron%2C_San_Fernando%2C_El_Salvador.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/El_Chorreron%2C_San_Fernando%2C_El_Salvador.jpg/330px-El_Chorreron%2C_San_Fernando%2C_El_Salvador.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/1/16/El_Chorreron%2C_San_Fernando%2C_El_Salvador.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:El_Chorreron,_San_Fernando,_El_Salvador.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         El Chorreron, El Salvador; tourism is the fastest-growing sector of the Salvadoran economy.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       El Salvador has promoted an open trade and investment environment, and has embarked on a wave of privatization extending to telecommunications, electricity distribution, banking, and pension funds. In late 2006, the government and the Millennium Challenge Corporation signed a five-year, $461 million compact to stimulate economic growth and reduce poverty in the country's northern region, the primary conflict zone during the civil war, through investments in education, public services, enterprise development, and transportation infrastructure. With the adoption of the US dollar as its currency in 2001, El Salvador lost control over monetary policy. Any counter-cyclical policy response to the downturn must be through fiscal policy, which is constrained by legislative requirements for a two-thirds majority to approve any international financing.
      </p>

      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Remittances_from_abroad">
        Remittances from abroad
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       El Salvador leads the region in remittances per capita, with inflows equivalent to nearly all export income; about a third of all households receive these financial inflows. Remittances from Salvadorans living and working in the United States, sent to family members in El Salvador, are a major source of foreign
       <a href="/wiki/Income" title="Income">
        income
       </a>
       and offset the substantial
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Trade_deficit" title="Trade deficit">
        trade deficit
       </a>
       of $4.12 billion. Remittances have increased steadily in the last decade, and reached an all-time high of $3.32 billion in 2006 (an increase of 17% over the previous year).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70">
        <a href="#cite_note-70">
         [70]
        </a>
       </sup>
       approximately 16.2% of
       <a href="/wiki/Gross_domestic_product" title="Gross domestic product">
        gross domestic product
       </a>
       (GDP).
      </p>
      <p>
       Remittances have had positive and negative effects on El Salvador. In 2005, the number of people living in
       <a href="/wiki/Extreme_poverty" title="Extreme poverty">
        extreme poverty
       </a>
       in El Salvador was 20%,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71">
        <a href="#cite_note-71">
         [71]
        </a>
       </sup>
       according to a United Nations Development Program report. Without remittances, the number of Salvadorans living in extreme poverty would rise to 37%. While Salvadoran education levels have gone up, wage expectations have risen faster than either skills or productivity. For example, some Salvadorans are no longer willing to take jobs that pay them less than what they receive monthly from family members abroad. This has led to an influx of Hondurans and Nicaraguans who are willing to work for the prevailing wage. Also, the local propensity for consumption over investment has increased.
      </p>
      <p>
       Money from
       <a href="/wiki/Remittance" title="Remittance">
        remittances
       </a>
       has also increased prices for certain commodities such as real estate. With much higher wages, many Salvadorans abroad can afford higher prices for houses in El Salvador than local Salvadorans, and thus push up the prices that all Salvadorans must pay.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72">
        <a href="#cite_note-72">
         [72]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Free_trade_agreements">
        Free trade agreements
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Torre_futura.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1024" data-file-width="768" height="293" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/Torre_futura.jpg/220px-Torre_futura.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/Torre_futura.jpg/330px-Torre_futura.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/Torre_futura.jpg/440px-Torre_futura.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Torre_futura.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Torre_Futura" title="Torre Futura">
          Torre Futura
         </a>
         at
         <a href="/wiki/World_Trade_Center_San_Salvador" title="World Trade Center San Salvador">
          World Trade Center San Salvador
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       In 2006, El Salvador was the first country to ratify the Central America-Dominican Republic Free Trade Agreement. CAFTA has bolstered exports of processed foods, sugar, and ethanol, and supported investment in the apparel sector, which faced Asian competition with the expiration of the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Multi-Fiber_Agreement" title="Multi-Fiber Agreement">
        Multi-Fiber Agreement
       </a>
       in 2005. In anticipation of the declines in the apparel sector's competitiveness, the previous administration sought to diversify the economy by promoting the country as a regional distribution and logistics hub, and by promoting tourism investment through tax incentives.
      </p>
      <p>
       There are a total of 15
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Free_trade_zone" title="Free trade zone">
        free trade zones
       </a>
       in El Salvador. El Salvador signed the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Central_American_Free_Trade_Agreement" title="Central American Free Trade Agreement">
        Central American Free Trade Agreement
       </a>
       (CAFTA) — negotiated by the five countries of Central America and the
       <a href="/wiki/Dominican_Republic" title="Dominican Republic">
        Dominican Republic
       </a>
       — with the United States in 2004. CAFTA requires that the Salvadoran government adopt policies that foster
       <a href="/wiki/Free_trade" title="Free trade">
        free trade
       </a>
       . El Salvador has signed free trade agreements with Mexico,
       <a href="/wiki/Chile" title="Chile">
        Chile
       </a>
       , the Dominican Republic, and
       <a href="/wiki/Panama" title="Panama">
        Panama
       </a>
       and increased its
       <a href="/wiki/Trade" title="Trade">
        trade
       </a>
       with those countries. El Salvador, Guatemala, Honduras, and Nicaragua also are negotiating a free trade agreement with Canada. In October 2007, these four countries and Costa Rica began free trade agreement negotiations with the European Union. Negotiations started in 2006 for a free trade agreement with
       <a href="/wiki/Colombia" title="Colombia">
        Colombia
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Official_corruption_and_foreign_investment">
        Official corruption and foreign investment
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       In an analysis of ARENA's electoral defeat in 2009, the U.S. Embassy in San Salvador pointed to official corruption under the Saca administration as a significant reason for public rejection of continued ARENA government. According to a secret diplomatic cable made public by WikiLeaks, "While the Salvadoran public may be inured to self-serving behavior by politicians, many in ARENA believe that the brazen manner in which Saca and his people are widely perceived to have used their positions for personal enrichment went beyond the pale. ARENA deputy Roberto d'Aubuisson, son of ARENA founder
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Roberto_d%27Aubuisson" title="Roberto d'Aubuisson">
        Roberto d'Aubuisson
       </a>
       , told [a U.S. diplomat] that Saca 'deliberately ignored' his Public Works Minister’s government contract kickbacks scheme, even after the case was revealed in the press. Furthermore, considerable evidence exists, including from U.S. business sources, that the Saca administration pushed laws and selectively enforced regulations with the specific intent to benefit Saca family business interests."
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73">
        <a href="#cite_note-73">
         [73]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Subsequent policies under Funes administrations improved El Salvador to foreign investment, and the World Bank in 2014 rated El Salvador 109, a little better than Belize (118) and Nicaragua (119) in the World Bank's annual "
       <a href="/wiki/Ease_of_doing_business_index" title="Ease of doing business index">
        Ease of doing business
       </a>
       " index.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74">
        <a href="#cite_note-74">
         [74]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       As per Santander Trade, a Spanish think tank in foreign investment, "Foreign investment into El Salvador has been steadily growing during the last few years. In 2013, the influx of FDI increased. Nevertheless, El Salvador receives less FDI than other countries of Central America. The government has made little progress in terms of improving the business climate. In addition to this, the limited size of its domestic market, weak infrastructures and institutions, as well as the high level of criminality have been real obstacles to investors. However, El Salvador is the second most "business friendly" country in South America in terms of business taxation. It also has a young and skilled labor force and a strategic geographical position. The country's membership in the DR-CAFTA, as well as its reinforced integration to the C4 countries (producers of cotton) should lead to an increase of FDI."
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75">
        <a href="#cite_note-75">
         [75]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Foreign companies have lately resorted to arbitration in international trade tribunals in total disagreement with Salvadoran government policies. In 2008, El Salvador sought international arbitration against Italy's Enel Green Power, on behalf of Salvadoran state-owned electric companies for a geothermal project Enel had invested in. Four years later, Enel indicated it would seek arbitration against El Salvador, blaming the government for technical problems that prevent it from completing its investment.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76">
        <a href="#cite_note-76">
         [76]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The government came to its defense claiming that Art 109 of the constitution does not allow any government (regardless of the party they belong), to privatize the resources of the national soil (in this case geothermic energy). The dispute came to an end in December 2014 when both parties came to a settlement, from which no details have been released. The small country had yielded to pressure from the Washington based powerful
       <a href="/wiki/International_Centre_for_Settlement_of_Investment_Disputes" title="International Centre for Settlement of Investment Disputes">
        ICSID
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77">
        <a href="#cite_note-77">
         [77]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The U.S. Embassy warned in 2009 that the Salvadoran government's populist policies of mandating artificially low electricity prices were damaging private sector profitability, including the interests of American investors in the energy sector.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ID_No._09SANSALVADOR1184_78-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-ID_No._09SANSALVADOR1184-78">
         [78]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The U.S. Embassy noted the corruption of El Salvador's judicial system and quietly urged American businesses to include "arbitration clauses, preferably with a foreign venue," when doing business in the country.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ID_No._09SANSALVADOR47_79-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-ID_No._09SANSALVADOR47-79">
         [79]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The U.S. Embassy warned in 2009 that the Salvadoran government's populist policies of mandating artificially low electricity prices were damaging private sector profitability, including the interests of American investors in the energy sector.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ID_No._09SANSALVADOR1184_78-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-ID_No._09SANSALVADOR1184-78">
         [78]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The U.S. Embassy noted the corruption of El Salvador's judicial system and quietly urged American businesses to include "arbitration clauses, preferably with a foreign venue," when doing business in the country.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ID_No._09SANSALVADOR47_79-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-ID_No._09SANSALVADOR47-79">
         [79]
        </a>
       </sup>
       On the other hand, a 2008 report by the
       <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Conference_on_Trade_and_Development" title="United Nations Conference on Trade and Development">
        United Nations Conference on Trade and Development
       </a>
       <a class="external autonumber" href="http://unctad.org/en/docs/diaepcb200920_en.pdf" rel="nofollow">
        [2]
       </a>
       indicates that one third of the generation of electricity in El Salvador was publicly owned while two thirds was in American hands and other foreign ownership. It is only natural for a small, under-developed country like El Salvador to subsidize some of the resources for the vast majority of its poor population.
      </p>
      <p>
       Although some events may have tarnished the image of the El Salvadoran government,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80">
        <a href="#cite_note-80">
         [80]
        </a>
       </sup>
       not everything is bad news. In terms of how people perceived the levels of public corruption in 2014, El Salvador ranks 80 out of 175 countries as per the Corruption Perception Index.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81">
        <a href="#cite_note-81">
         [81]
        </a>
       </sup>
       El Salvador's rating compares relatively well with Panama (94 of 175) and Costa Rica (47 of 175).
      </p>
      <p>
       <b>
        Pacific Rim Mining Corp. sues El Salvador for $301 million
       </b>
      </p>
      <p>
       According to the Center for International Environmental Law, "the Pacific Rim Mining Corporation (Pac Rim) has attempted to bypass El Salvador’s environmental protection laws using investor-state dispute settlement (ISDS) to sue the country for $77 million USD – as of July 2014 now more than $300 million USD – under the US-Central America Free Trade Agreement (CAFTA). El Salvador has upheld a nationally supported mining moratorium and is now defending itself against the Pac Rim allegations.".
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82">
        <a href="#cite_note-82">
         [82]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       After having lost its intent to sue under CAFTA-DR, in 2012, The World Bank arbitration panel ruled that the Canada-based company cannot use CAFTA, but the case could be pursued under Salvadoran national investment law under
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/International_Center_for_the_Settlement_of_Investment_Disputes" title="International Center for the Settlement of Investment Disputes">
        International Center for the Settlement of Investment Disputes
       </a>
       . The Canadian owned company, then opened a subsidiary in the United States and continued suing. In September 2014, a tribunal of the World Bank's International, the
       <a href="/wiki/International_Centre_for_Settlement_of_Investment_Disputes" title="International Centre for Settlement of Investment Disputes">
        ICSID
       </a>
       was supposed to rule in the dispute. As of April 2015, no news on the ruling have been released, but the Salvadoran government is confident that it will be favorable. The government has received overwhelming worldwide and local support for its cause, trying to ban mining in Salvadoran territory. Costa Rica has banned mining on Costa Rican soil. There is a strong popular rejection of mining companies in El Salvador due to the scarcity of local resources; mining companies are not traditionally perceived in a favorable light in El Salvador, (Cabanas Department) due to their poor environmental record. Pacific Rim is not the best example of a good friend of the environment. The news of a powerful corporation suing a small country has generated considerable controversy worldwide. Robin Broad and John Cavanagh of the
       <a href="/wiki/Foreign_Policy_in_Focus" title="Foreign Policy in Focus">
        Foreign Policy in Focus
       </a>
       , an international network of policy analysts and advocates, presented a first hand report on the situation.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83">
        <a href="#cite_note-83">
         [83]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The authors actually traveled to El Salvador and interviewed the locals who are directly involved in the drama. According to an
       <a href="/wiki/Institute_for_Policy_Studies" title="Institute for Policy Studies">
        IPS
       </a>
       article of September, 2014, "Last year,
       <a href="/wiki/OceanaGold" title="OceanaGold">
        OceanaGold
       </a>
       purchased Pacific Rim, despite the latter’s primary asset being the El Salvador gold-mining project, which has never been allowed to go forward. Although OceanaGold did not respond to a request for comment for this story, last year the company noted that it would continue with the arbitration case while also seeking "a negotiated resolution to the … permitting impasse". For its part, the Salvadoran government says it has halted the permitting process not only over environmental and health concerns but also over procedural matters. While these include Pacific Rim’s failure to abide by certain reporting requirements, the company also appears not to have gained important local approvals. Under Salvadoran law, an extractive company needs to gain titles, or local permission, for any lands it wants to develop. Yet Pacific Rim had such access to just 13 percent of the lands covered by its proposal, according to Oxfam America, a humanitarian and advocacy group.".
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84">
        <a href="#cite_note-84">
         [84]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Tourism">
        Tourism
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Further information:
       <a href="/wiki/Tourism_in_El_Salvador" title="Tourism in El Salvador">
        Tourism in El Salvador
       </a>
      </div>
