       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Moncagua_El_Salvador.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1200" data-file-width="1600" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/Moncagua_El_Salvador.jpg/220px-Moncagua_El_Salvador.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/Moncagua_El_Salvador.jpg/330px-Moncagua_El_Salvador.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/Moncagua_El_Salvador.jpg/440px-Moncagua_El_Salvador.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Moncagua_El_Salvador.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Moncagua" title="Moncagua">
          Moncagua
         </a>
         , San Miguel
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       It was estimated that 1,394,000 international tourists would visit El Salvador in 2014.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85">
        <a href="#cite_note-85">
         [85]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Tourism contributed US$855.5 million to El Salvador's GDP in 2013. This represented 3.5% of total GDP.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wttc.org_86-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-wttc.org-86">
         [86]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Tourism directly supported 80,500 jobs in 2013. This represented 3.1% of total employment in El Salvador.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wttc.org_86-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-wttc.org-86">
         [86]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In 2013, tourism indirectly supported 210,000 jobs, representing 8.1% of total employment in El Salvador.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wttc.org_86-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-wttc.org-86">
         [86]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The airport serving international flights in El Salvador is
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Comalapa_International_Airport" title="Comalapa International Airport">
        Comalapa International Airport
       </a>
       . This airport is located about 40 km (25 mi) southeast of San Salvador.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87">
        <a href="#cite_note-87">
         [87]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Surfing_in_El_Salvador_by_L._E._MacDonald.png">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="534" data-file-width="1024" height="115" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Surfing_in_El_Salvador_by_L._E._MacDonald.png/220px-Surfing_in_El_Salvador_by_L._E._MacDonald.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Surfing_in_El_Salvador_by_L._E._MacDonald.png/330px-Surfing_in_El_Salvador_by_L._E._MacDonald.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Surfing_in_El_Salvador_by_L._E._MacDonald.png/440px-Surfing_in_El_Salvador_by_L._E._MacDonald.png 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Surfing_in_El_Salvador_by_L._E._MacDonald.png" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         El Salvador has surf tourism due to large waves from the Pacific Ocean.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Most North American and European tourists seek out El Salvador's beaches and nightlife. Besides these two attractions, El Salvador's tourism landscape is slightly different from those of other Central American countries. Because of its geographic size and urbanization there are not many nature-themed tourist destinations such as ecotours or archaeological sites open to the public.
       <a href="/wiki/Surfing" title="Surfing">
        Surfing
       </a>
       is a natural tourism sector that has gained popularity in recent years as Salvadoran beaches have become increasingly popular.
      </p>
      <p>
       Surfers visit many beaches on the coast of La Libertad and the east end of El Salvador, finding surfing spots that are not yet overcrowded. The use of the
       <a href="/wiki/United_States_dollar" title="United States dollar">
        United States dollar
       </a>
       as Salvadoran currency and direct flights of 4 to 6 hours from most cities in the United States are factors that attract American tourists. Urbanization and
       <a href="/wiki/Americanization" title="Americanization">
        Americanization
       </a>
       of Salvadoran culture has also led to the abundance of American-style malls, stores, and restaurants in the three main urban areas, especially greater San Salvador.
      </p>
      <p>
       According to the El Salvadoran newspaper
       <i>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/El_Diario_De_Hoy" title="El Diario De Hoy">
         El Diario De Hoy
        </a>
       </i>
       , the top 10 attractions are: the coastal beaches,
       <a href="/wiki/La_Libertad,_La_Libertad" title="La Libertad, La Libertad">
        La Libertad
       </a>
       , Ruta Las Flores,
       <a href="/wiki/Suchitoto" title="Suchitoto">
        Suchitoto
       </a>
       , Playa Las Flores in
       <a href="/wiki/San_Miguel,_El_Salvador" title="San Miguel, El Salvador">
        San Miguel
       </a>
       , La Palma,
       <a href="/wiki/Santa_Ana_Volcano" title="Santa Ana Volcano">
        Santa Ana
       </a>
       (location of the country's highest volcano),
       <a href="/wiki/Nahuizalco" title="Nahuizalco">
        Nahuizalco
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Apaneca" title="Apaneca">
        Apaneca
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Juayua" title="Juayua">
        Juayua
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/San_Ignacio,_Chalatenango" title="San Ignacio, Chalatenango">
        San Ignacio
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88">
        <a href="#cite_note-88">
         [88]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Infrastructure">
        Infrastructure
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Hub_de_Avianca_en_El_Salvador.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="358" data-file-width="828" height="95" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/93/Hub_de_Avianca_en_El_Salvador.jpg/220px-Hub_de_Avianca_en_El_Salvador.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/93/Hub_de_Avianca_en_El_Salvador.jpg/330px-Hub_de_Avianca_en_El_Salvador.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/93/Hub_de_Avianca_en_El_Salvador.jpg/440px-Hub_de_Avianca_en_El_Salvador.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Hub_de_Avianca_en_El_Salvador.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         El Salvador International Airport
         <a href="/wiki/Monse%C3%B1or_%C3%93scar_Arnulfo_Romero_International_Airport" title="Monseñor Óscar Arnulfo Romero International Airport">
          Monseñor Óscar Arnulfo Romero International Airport
         </a>
         at night
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Boulevard_mosenor_romero.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="403" data-file-width="403" height="220" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/Boulevard_mosenor_romero.jpg/220px-Boulevard_mosenor_romero.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/Boulevard_mosenor_romero.jpg/330px-Boulevard_mosenor_romero.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/d/da/Boulevard_mosenor_romero.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Boulevard_mosenor_romero.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/RN-21_(Boulevard_Diego_Holguin)" title="RN-21 (Boulevard Diego Holguin)">
          RN-21 (Boulevard Diego Holguin)
         </a>
         , now known as Boulevard Oscar Romero, was El Salvador's and one of Central America's first freeways.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Water_supply_and_sanitation">
        Water supply and sanitation
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Water_supply_and_sanitation_in_El_Salvador" title="Water supply and sanitation in El Salvador">
        Water supply and sanitation in El Salvador
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       The level of access to
       <a href="/wiki/Water_supply" title="Water supply">
        water supply
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Sanitation" title="Sanitation">
        sanitation
       </a>
       has been increased significantly. A 2015 conducted study by the University of North Carolina called El Salvador the country that has achieved the greatest progress in the world in terms of increased access to water supply and sanitation and the reduction of inequity in access between urban and rural areas.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89">
        <a href="#cite_note-89">
         [89]
        </a>
       </sup>
       However, water resources are seriously polluted and a large part of the wastewater discharged into the environment without any
       <a href="/wiki/Wastewater_treatment" title="Wastewater treatment">
        treatment
       </a>
       . Institutionally a single public institution is both de facto in charge of setting sector policy and of being the main service provider. Attempts at reforming and modernizing the sector through new laws have not borne fruit over the past 20 years.
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">
        Demographics
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_El_Salvador" title="Demographics of El Salvador">
        Demographics of El Salvador
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       El Salvador's population was 6,344,722 in 2016,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UN_WPP_3-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-UN_WPP-3">
         [3]
        </a>
       </sup>
       compared to 2,200,000 in 1950. In 2010 the percentage of the population below the age of 15 was 32.1%, 61% were between 15 and 65 years of age, while 6.9% were 65 years or older.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WPP_2012_90-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-WPP_2012-90">
         [90]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The capital city of San Salvador has a population of about 2.1 million people. An estimated 42% of El Salvador's population live in rural areas.
       <a href="/wiki/Urbanization" title="Urbanization">
        Urbanization
       </a>
       has expanded at a phenomenal rate in El Salvador since the 1960s, with millions moving to the cities and creating associated problems for urban planning and services.
      </p>
      <p>
       There are up to 100,000
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nicaraguan" title="Nicaraguan">
        Nicaraguans
       </a>
       living in El Salvador.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91">
        <a href="#cite_note-91">
         [91]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Ethnic_groups">
        Ethnic groups
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Potada.JPG">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="400" data-file-width="300" height="227" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/Potada.JPG/170px-Potada.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/Potada.JPG/255px-Potada.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/f/ff/Potada.JPG 2x" width="170"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Potada.JPG" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Salvadoran model
         <a href="/wiki/Irma_Dimas" title="Irma Dimas">
          Irma Dimas
         </a>
         was crowned Miss El Salvador in 2005. She made headlines recently for her entry into Salvadoran politics.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       El Salvador's population is composed of
       <a href="/wiki/Mestizo" title="Mestizo">
        Mestizos
       </a>
       , whites, and indigenous peoples. Eighty-six percent of Salvadorans are of mestizo ancestry, having mixed indigenous and European ancestry.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cia_92-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-cia-92">
         [92]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In the mestizo population, Salvadorans who are racially European, especially Mediterranean, as well as
       <a href="/wiki/Afro-Salvadoran" title="Afro-Salvadoran">
        Afro-Salvadoran
       </a>
       , and the indigenous people in El Salvador who do not speak indigenous languages or have an indigenous culture, all identify themselves as being culturally mestizo.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93">
        <a href="#cite_note-93">
         [93]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       12.7% of Salvadorans are
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/White_Latin_American" title="White Latin American">
        white
       </a>
       . A majority of
       <a href="/wiki/Central_Europe" title="Central Europe">
        Central European
       </a>
       immigrants in El Salvador arrived during World War II as refugees from the
       <a href="/wiki/Czech_Republic" title="Czech Republic">
        Czech Republic
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Germany" title="Germany">
        Germany
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Hungary" title="Hungary">
        Hungary
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Poland" title="Poland">
        Poland
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Switzerland" title="Switzerland">
        Switzerland
       </a>
       . There are also a small community of
       <a href="/wiki/Jews" title="Jews">
        Jews
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Palestinian_Christians" title="Palestinian Christians">
        Palestinian Christians
       </a>
       , and Arab
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Muslims" title="Muslims">
        Muslims
       </a>
       (in particular
       <a href="/wiki/Palestinian_Salvadoran" title="Palestinian Salvadoran">
        Palestinians
       </a>
       ).
      </p>
      <p>
       0.23% of the population are of full indigenous origin, the ethnic groups are Kakawira which represents 0.07% of the total country's population, then (
       <a href="/wiki/Pipil_people" title="Pipil people">
        Pipil
       </a>
       ) 0.06%, (
       <a href="/wiki/Lenca_people" title="Lenca people">
        Lenca
       </a>
       ) 0.04% and others minors groups 0.06%. Very few Amerindians have retained their customs and traditions, having over time assimilated into the dominant Mestizo/Spanish culture.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94">
        <a href="#cite_note-94">
         [94]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       There is a small
       <a href="/wiki/Afro-Salvadoran" title="Afro-Salvadoran">
        Afro-Salvadoran
       </a>
       that is 0.13% of the total population, with Blacks having traditionally been prevented from immigrating via government policies.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95">
        <a href="#cite_note-95">
         [95]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-B_96-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-B-96">
         [96]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Among the immigrant groups in El Salvador, Palestinian Christians stand out.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97">
        <a href="#cite_note-97">
         [97]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Though few in number, their descendants have attained great economic and political power in the country, as evidenced by the election of ex-president
       <a href="/wiki/Antonio_Saca" title="Antonio Saca">
        Antonio Saca
       </a>
       , whose opponent in the 2004 election,
       <a href="/wiki/Schafik_Handal" title="Schafik Handal">
        Schafik Handal
       </a>
       , was also of Palestinian descent, and the flourishing commercial, industrial, and construction firms owned by this ethnic group.
      </p>
      <p>
       As of 2004
       <sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;">
        <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=El_Salvador&amp;action=edit">
         [update]
        </a>
       </sup>
       , there were approximately 3.2 million Salvadorans living outside El Salvador, with the United States traditionally being the destination of choice for Salvadoran economic migrants. By 2012, there were about 2.0 million Salvadoran immigrants and Americans of Salvadoran descent in the U.S.,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2012AmericanCommunitySurvey_98-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-2012AmericanCommunitySurvey-98">
         [98]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99">
        <a href="#cite_note-99">
         [99]
        </a>
       </sup>
       making them the sixth largest immigrant group in the country.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100">
        <a href="#cite_note-100">
         [100]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The second destinatation of Salvadorans living outside is
       <a href="/wiki/Guatemala" title="Guatemala">
        Guatemala
       </a>
       , with more than 111,000 persons, mainly in
       <a href="/wiki/Guatemala_City" title="Guatemala City">
        Guatemala City
       </a>
       . Salvadorans also live in other nearby countries such as
       <a href="/wiki/Belize" title="Belize">
        Belize
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Honduras" title="Honduras">
        Honduras
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Nicaragua" title="Nicaragua">
        Nicaragua
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101">
        <a href="#cite_note-101">
         [101]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Other countries with notable Salvadoran communities include Canada, Mexico, the United Kingdom (including the
       <a href="/wiki/Cayman_Islands" title="Cayman Islands">
        Cayman Islands
       </a>
       ), Sweden, Brazil, Italy, Colombia, and Australia.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Languages">
        Languages
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       Spanish is the official language and is spoken by virtually all inhabitants. Some indigenous people speak their native tongues (such as
       <a href="/wiki/Pipil_language" title="Pipil language">
        Nawat
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Mayan_languages" title="Mayan languages">
        Maya
       </a>
       ), but indigenous Salvadorans who do not identify as mestizo constitute only 1% of the country's population. However, all of them can speak Spanish.
       <a href="/wiki/Q%27eqchi%27_language" title="Q'eqchi' language">
        Q'eqchi'
       </a>
       is spoken by immigrants of
       <a href="/wiki/Guatemala" title="Guatemala">
        Guatemalan
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Belize" title="Belize">
        Belizean
       </a>
       indigenous people living in El Salvador. There have also been recent large migrations of
       <a href="/wiki/Hondurans" title="Hondurans">
        Hondurans
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Nicaraguans" title="Nicaraguans">
        Nicaraguans
       </a>
       into the country.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102">
        <a href="#cite_note-102">
         [102]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The local Spanish
       <a href="/wiki/Vernacular" title="Vernacular">
        vernacular
       </a>
       is called
       <i>
        Caliche
       </i>
       . Salvadorans use
       <a href="/wiki/Voseo" title="Voseo">
        voseo
       </a>
       , which is also used in
       <a href="/wiki/Argentina" title="Argentina">
        Argentina
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Costa_Rica" title="Costa Rica">
        Costa Rica
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Nicaragua" title="Nicaragua">
        Nicaragua
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Uruguay" title="Uruguay">
        Uruguay
       </a>
       . This refers to the use of "vos" as the second person pronoun, instead of "tú". "Caliche" is considered informal, and a few people choose not to use it.
       <a href="/wiki/Pipil_language" title="Pipil language">
        Nawat
       </a>
       is an indigenous language that has survived, though it is only used by small communities of some elderly Salvadorans in western El Salvador.
      </p>
      <h3>

      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">
        Religion
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Religion_in_El_Salvador" title="Religion in El Salvador">
        Religion in El Salvador
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="barbox tright" style="overflow-x: auto;">
       <div style="border:1px solid silver; font-size:88%; padding:0.4em; width:auto; background: white;">
        <table style="border-collapse:collapse; width:100%;">
         <tr style="background:#DDD">

          </td>

          </td>

           </a>

       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The majority of the population in El Salvador is
       <a href="/wiki/Christian" title="Christian">
        Christian
       </a>
       .
       <a href="/wiki/Catholic_Church" title="Catholic Church">
        Roman Catholics
       </a>
       (47%) and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Protestants" title="Protestants">
        Protestants
       </a>
       (33%) are the two major denominations in the country.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IRFR2012_104-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-IRFR2012-104">
         [104]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Those not affiliated with any religious group amount to 17% of the population.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IRFR2012_104-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-IRFR2012-104">
         [104]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The remainder of the population (3%) is made up of
       <a href="/wiki/Jehovah%27s_Witnesses" title="Jehovah's Witnesses">
        Jehovah's Witnesses
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hare_Krishnas" title="Hare Krishnas">
        Hare Krishnas
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Muslims" title="Muslims">
        Muslims
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Jews" title="Jews">
        Jews
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Buddhists" title="Buddhists">
        Buddhists
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Latter-day_Saints" title="Latter-day Saints">
        Latter-day Saints
       </a>
       , and those adhering to indigenous religious beliefs.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IRFR2012_104-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-IRFR2012-104">
         [104]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The number of evangelicals in the country is growing rapidly.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105">
        <a href="#cite_note-105">
         [105]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Health">
        Health
       </span>
      </h2>
      <p>
       For the period between 2005 and 2010, El Salvador had the third lowest
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_birth_rate" title="List of countries by birth rate">
        birth rate
       </a>
       in Central America, with 22.8 births per 1,000. However, during the same period, it had the highest
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_death_rate" title="List of countries by death rate">
        death rate
       </a>
       in Central America, 5.9 deaths per 1,000. According to the most recent
       <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">
        United Nations
       </a>
       survey, life expectancy for men was 68 years and 74 years for women. Healthy life expectancy was 57 for males and 62 for females in 2003.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106">
        <a href="#cite_note-106">
         [106]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Education">
        Education
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Further information:
       <a href="/wiki/Education_in_El_Salvador" title="Education in El Salvador">
        Education in El Salvador
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Asociaci%C3%B3n_Salvadore%C3%B1a_de_Astronom%C3%ADa_Observatorio_%22Dr._Prudencio_Llach%22.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="4000" data-file-width="6016" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/Asociaci%C3%B3n_Salvadore%C3%B1a_de_Astronom%C3%ADa_Observatorio_%22Dr._Prudencio_Llach%22.jpg/220px-Asociaci%C3%B3n_Salvadore%C3%B1a_de_Astronom%C3%ADa_Observatorio_%22Dr._Prudencio_Llach%22.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/Asociaci%C3%B3n_Salvadore%C3%B1a_de_Astronom%C3%ADa_Observatorio_%22Dr._Prudencio_Llach%22.jpg/330px-Asociaci%C3%B3n_Salvadore%C3%B1a_de_Astronom%C3%ADa_Observatorio_%22Dr._Prudencio_Llach%22.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/Asociaci%C3%B3n_Salvadore%C3%B1a_de_Astronom%C3%ADa_Observatorio_%22Dr._Prudencio_Llach%22.jpg/440px-Asociaci%C3%B3n_Salvadore%C3%B1a_de_Astronom%C3%ADa_Observatorio_%22Dr._Prudencio_Llach%22.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Asociaci%C3%B3n_Salvadore%C3%B1a_de_Astronom%C3%ADa_Observatorio_%22Dr._Prudencio_Llach%22.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Dr. Prudencio Llach Observatory
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The public education system in El Salvador is severely lacking in resources. Class sizes in public schools can be as large as 50 children per classroom. Salvadorans who can afford the cost often choose to send their children to private schools, which are regarded as being better-quality than public schools. Most private schools follow American, European or other advanced systems. Lower-income families are forced to rely on public education.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2018)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Education in El Salvador is free through high school. After nine years of basic education (elementary–middle school), students have the option of a two-year high school or a three-year high school. A two-year high school prepares the student for transfer to a university. A three-year high school allows the student to graduate and enter the workforce in a vocational career, or to transfer to a university to further their education in their chosen field.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107">
        <a href="#cite_note-107">
         [107]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/List_of_universities_in_El_Salvador" title="List of universities in El Salvador">
        Universities in El Salvador
       </a>
       include a central public institution, the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Universidad_de_El_Salvador" title="Universidad de El Salvador">
        Universidad de El Salvador
       </a>
       , and many other specialised private universities.
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Crime">
        Crime
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Crime_in_El_Salvador" title="Crime in El Salvador">
        Crime in El Salvador
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:PNC-02N_MD_Helicopters_MD520N_El_Salvador_Policia_(7486576752).jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1536" data-file-width="2304" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/PNC-02N_MD_Helicopters_MD520N_El_Salvador_Policia_%287486576752%29.jpg/220px-PNC-02N_MD_Helicopters_MD520N_El_Salvador_Policia_%287486576752%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/PNC-02N_MD_Helicopters_MD520N_El_Salvador_Policia_%287486576752%29.jpg/330px-PNC-02N_MD_Helicopters_MD520N_El_Salvador_Policia_%287486576752%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/PNC-02N_MD_Helicopters_MD520N_El_Salvador_Policia_%287486576752%29.jpg/440px-PNC-02N_MD_Helicopters_MD520N_El_Salvador_Policia_%287486576752%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:PNC-02N_MD_Helicopters_MD520N_El_Salvador_Policia_(7486576752).jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/National_Civil_Police_of_El_Salvador" title="National Civil Police of El Salvador">
          National Civil Police of El Salvador
         </a>
         helicopter
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Since the early twenty-first century, El Salvador has experienced high crime rates, including gang-related crimes and
       <a href="/wiki/Juvenile_delinquency" title="Juvenile delinquency">
        juvenile delinquency
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108">
        <a href="#cite_note-108">
         [108]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Some say that this was a result of the deportation of thousands of Salvadorans from the U.S, the majority of whom were members of
       <a href="/wiki/MS-13" title="MS-13">
        MS-13
       </a>
       (Mara Salvatrucha, or La Mara), in the mid-1990s. The gangs in which Salvadorans had been involved in the United States began to show up in El Salvador.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109">
        <a href="#cite_note-109">
         [109]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       El Salvador has one of the highest murder rates in the world.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110">
        <a href="#cite_note-110">
         [110]
        </a>
       </sup>
       El Salvador is also considered an epicenter of a gang crisis, along with
       <a href="/wiki/Guatemala" title="Guatemala">
        Guatemala
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Honduras" title="Honduras">
        Honduras
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FAS_111-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FAS-111">
         [111]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In response to this, the government has set up countless programs to try to guide the youth away from gang membership; so far its efforts have not produced any quick results. One of the government programs was a gang reform called "
       <a href="/wiki/La_Mano_Dura" title="La Mano Dura">
        Super Mano Dura
       </a>
       " (Super Firm Hand). Super Mano Dura had little success and was highly criticized by the
       <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">
        UN
       </a>
       . It saw temporary success in 2004 but then saw a rise in crime after 2005. In 2004, the rate of intentional homicides per 100,000 citizens was 41, with 60% of the homicides committed being
       <a href="/wiki/Gang" title="Gang">
        gang
       </a>
       -related.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FAS_111-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-FAS-111">
         [111]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The Salvadoran government reported that the Super Mano Dura gang legislation led to a 14% drop in murders in 2004. However, El Salvador had 66 homicides per 100,000 inhabitants in 2012, more than triple the rate in Mexico that year.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NYRB_112-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-NYRB-112">
         [112]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-113">
        <a href="#cite_note-113">
         [113]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-114">
        <a href="#cite_note-114">
         [114]
        </a>
       </sup>
       There are an estimated 25,000 gang members at large in El Salvador with another 9,000 in prison.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NYRB_112-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-NYRB-112">
         [112]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The most well-known gangs, called "
       <a href="/wiki/Mara_(gang)" title="Mara (gang)">
        maras
       </a>
       " in colloquial Spanish, are
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mara_Salvatrucha" title="Mara Salvatrucha">
        Mara Salvatrucha
       </a>
       and their rivals
       <a href="/wiki/18th_Street_gang" title="18th Street gang">
        Calle 18
       </a>
       . Maras are hunted by
       <a href="/wiki/Death_squad" title="Death squad">
        death squads
       </a>
       including
       <a href="/wiki/Sombra_Negra" title="Sombra Negra">
        Sombra Negra
       </a>
       . New rivals also include the rising mara, The Rebels 13.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-115">
        <a href="#cite_note-115">
         [115]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       As of March 2012, El Salvador has seen a 40% drop in crime due to what the Salvadoran government called a gang truce; however, extortions affecting small businesses are not taken into account. In early 2012, there were on average of 16 killings per day; in late March of that year that number dropped to fewer than 5 per day. On April 14, 2012 for the first time in over 3 years there were no killings in El Salvador.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-116">
        <a href="#cite_note-116">
         [116]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Overall, there were 411 killings in January 2012, and in March the number was 188, more than a 40% reduction,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-117">
        <a href="#cite_note-117">
         [117]
        </a>
       </sup>
       while crime in neighboring Honduras had risen to an all-time high.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-118">
        <a href="#cite_note-118">
         [118]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In 2014, crime rose 56% in El Salvador, with the government attributing the rise to a break in the truce between the two major gangs in El Salvador, which began having turf wars.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-119">
        <a href="#cite_note-119">
         [119]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Presently, the Alto al Crimen or
       <a href="/wiki/Crime_Stoppers" title="Crime Stoppers">
        Crime Stoppers
       </a>
       program is in operation and provides financial rewards for information leading to the capture of gang leadership. The reward often ranges between $100 and $500
       <a href="/wiki/United_States_dollar" title="United States dollar">
        US Dollars
       </a>
       per call.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-120">
        <a href="#cite_note-120">
         [120]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">
        Culture
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_El_Salvador" title="Culture of El Salvador">
        Culture of El Salvador
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Monumento_al_Salvador_del_Mundo_2.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2432" data-file-width="4320" height="124" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Monumento_al_Salvador_del_Mundo_2.jpg/220px-Monumento_al_Salvador_del_Mundo_2.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Monumento_al_Salvador_del_Mundo_2.jpg/330px-Monumento_al_Salvador_del_Mundo_2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Monumento_al_Salvador_del_Mundo_2.jpg/440px-Monumento_al_Salvador_del_Mundo_2.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Monumento_al_Salvador_del_Mundo_2.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         The iconic statue of Christ on the globe sphere of planet earth is part of the
         <a href="/wiki/Monumento_al_Divino_Salvador_del_Mundo" title="Monumento al Divino Salvador del Mundo">
          Monumento al Divino Salvador del Mundo
         </a>
         (Monument to the Divine Savior of the world) on Plaza El Salvador del Mundo (The Savior of the World Plaza), a landmark located in the country's capital, San Salvador.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/Mestizo" title="Mestizo">
        Mestizo
       </a>
       culture dominates the country, heavy in both Native American Indigenous and European Spanish influences. A new composite population was formed as a result of intermarrying between the native
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mesoamerican" title="Mesoamerican">
        Mesoamerican
       </a>
       population of Cuzcatlan with the European settlers. The
       <a href="/wiki/Catholic_Church" title="Catholic Church">
        Catholic Church
       </a>
       plays an important role in the Salvadoran culture.
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Archbishop_%C3%93scar_Romero" title="Archbishop Óscar Romero">
        Archbishop Óscar Romero
       </a>
       is a national hero for his role in resisting human rights violations that were occurring in the lead-up to the Salvadoran Civil War.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Eaton_121-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Eaton-121">
         [121]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Significant foreign personalities in El Salvador were the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jesuit" title="Jesuit">
        Jesuit
       </a>
       priests and professors
       <a href="/wiki/Ignacio_Ellacur%C3%ADa" title="Ignacio Ellacuría">
        Ignacio Ellacuría
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Ignacio_Mart%C3%ADn-Bar%C3%B3" title="Ignacio Martín-Baró">
        Ignacio Martín-Baró
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Segundo_Montes" title="Segundo Montes">
        Segundo Montes
       </a>
       , who were murdered in 1989 by the Salvadoran Army during the height of the civil war.
      </p>
      <p>
       Painting, ceramics and textiles are the principal manual artistic mediums. Writers
       <a href="/wiki/Francisco_Gavidia" title="Francisco Gavidia">
        Francisco Gavidia
       </a>
       (1863–1955),
       <a href="/wiki/Salarru%C3%A9" title="Salarrué">
        Salarrué
       </a>
       (Salvador Salazar Arrué) (1899–1975),
       <a href="/wiki/Claudia_Lars" title="Claudia Lars">
        Claudia Lars
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Alfredo_Espino" title="Alfredo Espino">
        Alfredo Espino
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Pedro_Geoffroy_Rivas" title="Pedro Geoffroy Rivas">
        Pedro Geoffroy Rivas
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Manlio_Argueta" title="Manlio Argueta">
        Manlio Argueta
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Roberto_Cea" title="José Roberto Cea">
        José Roberto Cea
       </a>
       , and poet
       <a href="/wiki/Roque_Dalton" title="Roque Dalton">
        Roque Dalton
       </a>
       are among the most important writers from El Salvador. Notable 20th-century personages include the late filmmaker Baltasar Polio, female film director
       <a href="/wiki/Patricia_Chica" title="Patricia Chica">
        Patricia Chica
       </a>
       , artist
       <a href="/wiki/Fernando_Llort" title="Fernando Llort">
        Fernando Llort
       </a>
       , and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Caricaturist" title="Caricaturist">
        caricaturist
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/To%C3%B1o_Salazar" title="Toño Salazar">
        Toño Salazar
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       Amongst the more renowned representatives of the graphic arts are the painters
       <a href="/wiki/Augusto_Crespin" title="Augusto Crespin">
        Augusto Crespin
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Noe_Canjura" title="Noe Canjura">
        Noe Canjura
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Carlos_Ca%C3%B1as" title="Carlos Cañas">
        Carlos Cañas
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Giovanni_Gil" title="Giovanni Gil">
        Giovanni Gil
       </a>
       , Julia Díaz, Mauricio Mejia, Maria Elena Palomo de Mejia,
       <a href="/wiki/Camilo_Minero" title="Camilo Minero">
        Camilo Minero
       </a>
       , Ricardo Carbonell, Roberto Huezo, Miguel Angel Cerna, (the painter and writer better known as MACLo), Esael Araujo, and many others. For more information on prominent citizens of El Salvador, check the
       <a href="/wiki/List_of_Salvadorans" title="List of Salvadorans">
        List of Salvadorans
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Public_holidays">
        Public holidays
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">

       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_festivals_in_El_Salvador&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="List of festivals in El Salvador (page does not exist)">
        List of festivals in El Salvador
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">

        </a>

        </div>
       </div>
      </div>

        </td>

        </td>
        <td>
         <a href="/wiki/Fiesta_de_las_Cruces" title="Fiesta de las Cruces">

         </a>
        </td>
        <td>
         <i>
          Día de la Cruz
         </i>
        </td>
        <td style="font-size:95%;">
         A celebration with precolonial origins, linked to the advent of the rainy season. People decorate a cross in their yards with fruit and garlands, in the belief that if they do not, the devil will appear and dance at their yard. They then go from house to house to kneel in front of the altar and make the sign of the cross.
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td>
         May 7
        </td>
        <td>
         Soldiers' Day
        </td>
        <td>
         <i>
          Día del Soldado
         </i>
        </td>
        <td style="font-size:95%;">
         Marks the founding of its armed forces in 1824.
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td>
         May 10
        </td>
        <td>
         Mothers' Day
        </td>
        <td>
         <i>
          Día de las Madres
         </i>
        </td>
        <td style="font-size:95%;">
         A day to celebrate motherhood, similar to many other countries Mother's Day.
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td>
         June 17
        </td>

         Father's Day
        </td>
        <td>
         <i>
          Día del Padre
         </i>
        </td>
        <td style="font-size:95%;">
         A day to celebrate fatherhood, similar to other countries Father's Day.
        </td>
       </tr>

        <td>

        </td>

         </i>

        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td>
         November 2
        </td>
        <td>
         <a href="/wiki/Day_of_the_Dead" title="Day of the Dead">

         </a>
        </td>
        <td>
         <i>
          El día de los difuntos
         </i>
        </td>
        <td style="font-size:95%;">
         A day when most people visit the tombs of deceased loved ones. (November 1 may be commemorated as well.)
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td>
         November 7–13
        </td>
        <td>
         National Festival Of Pupusa
        </td>
        <td>
         <i>
          Festival Nacional De La Pupusa
         </i>
        </td>
        <td style="font-size:95%;">
         This week is the national commemoration of the national food (
         <i>
          Pupusa
         </i>
         ).
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td>
         November 21
        </td>
        <td>
         Queen of the Peace Day
        </td>
        <td>
         <i>
          Dia de la Reina de la Paz
         </i>
        </td>
        <td style="font-size:95%;">
         Day of the Queen of Peace, the patron saint. Also celebrated, the San Miguel Carnival, (carnaval de San Miguel), celebrated in San Miguel City, similar to Mardi Gras of New Orleans, where one can enjoy about 45 music bands on the street.
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td>
         December 25
        </td>
        <td>
         Christmas Day (Celebrated Dec. 24th)
        </td>
        <td>
         <i>
          Noche Buena
         </i>
        </td>
        <td style="font-size:95%;">
         In many communities, December 24 (
         <a href="/wiki/Christmas_Eve" title="Christmas Eve">
          Christmas Eve
         </a>
         ) is the major day of celebration, often to the point that it is considered the actual day of
         <i>
          Navidad
         </i>
         — with December 25 serving as a day of rest.
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td>
         December 31
        </td>
        <td>
         <a href="/wiki/New_Year%27s_Eve" title="New Year's Eve">
          New Year's Eve
         </a>
        </td>
        <td>
         <i>
          Fin de año
         </i>
        </td>
        <td style="font-size:95%;">
         The final day of the Gregorian year, and the day before New Year's Day is celebrated in El Salvador with family reunions.
        </td>
       </tr>

      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Cuisine">
        Cuisine
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Salvadoran_cuisine" title="Salvadoran cuisine">
        Salvadoran cuisine
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Plain_pupusas_revueltas.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2000" data-file-width="3008" height="199" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/Plain_pupusas_revueltas.jpg/300px-Plain_pupusas_revueltas.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/Plain_pupusas_revueltas.jpg/450px-Plain_pupusas_revueltas.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/Plain_pupusas_revueltas.jpg/600px-Plain_pupusas_revueltas.jpg 2x" width="300"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Plain_pupusas_revueltas.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <i>
          Pupusas
         </i>
         , the national and most famous dish of El Salvador.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Sopa_de_pata.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1800" data-file-width="2459" height="161" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Sopa_de_pata.jpg/220px-Sopa_de_pata.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Sopa_de_pata.jpg/330px-Sopa_de_pata.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Sopa_de_pata.jpg/440px-Sopa_de_pata.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Sopa_de_pata.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <i>
          <a href="/wiki/Sopa_de_pata" title="Sopa de pata">
           Sopa de pata
          </a>
         </i>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       One of El Salvador's notable dishes is the
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Pupusa" title="Pupusa">
         pupusa
        </a>
       </i>
       .
       <i>
        Pupusas
       </i>
       are handmade corn tortillas (made of
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Masa" title="Masa">
         masa de maíz
        </a>
       </i>
       or
       <i>
        masa de arroz
       </i>
       , a maize or rice flour dough used in
       <a href="/wiki/Latin_American_cuisine" title="Latin American cuisine">
        Latin American cuisine
       </a>
       ) stuffed with one or more of the following: cheese (usually a soft Salvadoran cheese such as
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Quesillo" title="Quesillo">
         quesillo
        </a>
       </i>
       , similar to mozzarella),
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Chicharr%C3%B3n" title="Chicharrón">
         chicharrón
        </a>
       </i>
       , or
       <a href="/wiki/Refried_beans" title="Refried beans">
        refried beans
       </a>
       . Sometimes the filling is
       <i>
        queso con loroco
       </i>
       (cheese combined with
       <i>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Loroco" title="Loroco">
         loroco
        </a>
       </i>
       , a vine flower bud native to Central America).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Elsalvador.com_122-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Elsalvador.com-122">
         [122]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       <i>
        Pupusas revueltas
       </i>
       are
       <i>
        pupusas
       </i>
       filled with beans, cheese and pork. There are also vegetarian options. Some adventurous restaurants even offer
       <i>
        pupusas
       </i>
       stuffed with shrimp or spinach. The name
       <i>
        pupusa
       </i>
       comes from the Pipil-Nahuatl word,
       <i>
        pupushahua
       </i>
       . The precise origins of the
       <i>
        pupusa
       </i>
       are debated, although its presence in El Salvador is known to predate the arrival of the Spaniards.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Elsalvador.com_122-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-Elsalvador.com-122">
         [122]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Two other typical Salvadoran dishes are
       <i>
        yuca frita
       </i>
       and
       <i>
        panes con pollo
       </i>
       .
       <i>
        Yuca frita
       </i>
       is deep fried
       <a href="/wiki/Cassava" title="Cassava">
        cassava
       </a>
       root served with
       <a href="/wiki/Curtido" title="Curtido">
        curtido
       </a>
       (a pickled cabbage, onion and carrot topping) and pork rinds with
       <i>
        pescaditas
       </i>
       (fried baby sardines). The Yuca is sometimes served boiled instead of fried.
       <i>
        Pan con pollo/pavo
       </i>
       (bread with chicken/turkey) are warm
       <a href="/wiki/Turkey_(bird)" title="Turkey (bird)">
        turkey
       </a>
       or
       <a href="/wiki/Chicken" title="Chicken">
        chicken
       </a>
       -filled submarine sandwiches. The bird is marinated and then roasted with
       <a href="/wiki/Pipil_people" title="Pipil people">
        Pipil
       </a>
       spices and handpulled. This sandwich is traditionally served with
       <a href="/wiki/Tomato" title="Tomato">
        tomato
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Watercress" title="Watercress">
        watercress
       </a>
       along with
       <a href="/wiki/Cucumber" title="Cucumber">
        cucumber
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Onion" title="Onion">
        onion
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Lettuce" title="Lettuce">
        lettuce
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Mayonnaise" title="Mayonnaise">
        mayonnaise
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Mustard_(condiment)" title="Mustard (condiment)">
        mustard
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       One of El Salvador's typical breakfasts is fried plantain, usually served with cream. It is common in Salvadoran restaurants and homes, including those of immigrants to the United States.
      </p>
      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/Alguashte" title="Alguashte">
        Alguashte
       </a>
       , a condiment made from dried, ground
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pepitas" title="Pepitas">
        pepitas
       </a>
       , is commonly incorporated into savoury and sweet Salvadoran dishes.
      </p>
      <p>
       "
       <i>
        Maria Luisa
       </i>
       " is a dessert commonly found in El Salvador. It is a layered cake that is soaked in orange marmalade and sprinkled with powdered sugar.
      </p>
      <p>
       A popular drink that Salvadorans enjoy is
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Horchata" title="Horchata">
         Horchata
        </a>
       </i>
       , a drink native to the
       <a href="/wiki/Valencian_Community" title="Valencian Community">
        Valencian Community
       </a>
       in Spain.
       <i>
        Horchata
       </i>
       is most commonly made of the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Morro_seed" title="Morro seed">
        morro seed
       </a>
       ground into a powder and added to milk or water, and sugar.
       <i>
        Horchata
       </i>
       is drank year-round, and can be drank at any time of day. It mostly is accompanied by a plate of
       <i>
        pupusas
       </i>
       or fried yuca.
       <i>
        Horchata
       </i>
       from El Salvador has a very distinct taste and is not to be confused with Mexican
       <i>
        horchata
       </i>
       , which is rice-based. Coffee is also a common morning beverage.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-123">
        <a href="#cite_note-123">
         [123]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Other popular drinks in El Salvador include
       <i>
        Ensalada
       </i>
       , a drink made of chopped fruit swimming in fruit juice, and
       <i>
        Kolachampan
       </i>
       , a sugar cane-flavored carbonated beverage.
      </p>
      <p>
       One of the most popular desserts is the cake
       <i>
        Pastel de tres leches
       </i>
       (Cake of three milks), consisting of three types of milk: evaporated milk, condensed milk, and cream.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Music">
        Music
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Music_of_El_Salvador" title="Music of El Salvador">
        Music of El Salvador
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       Salvadoran music is a mixture of indigenous
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lenca" title="Lenca">
        Lenca
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Maya_peoples" title="Maya peoples">
        Maya
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Cacaopera_people" title="Cacaopera people">
        Cacaopera
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pipils" title="Pipils">
        Pipil
       </a>
       and Spanish influences. Music includes religious songs (mostly used to celebrate
       <a href="/wiki/Christmas" title="Christmas">
        Christmas
       </a>
       and other
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Religious_holiday" title="Religious holiday">
        holidays
       </a>
       , especially
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Feast_day" title="Feast day">
        feast days
       </a>
       of the
       <a href="/wiki/Saint" title="Saint">
        saints
       </a>
       ). Satirical and rural lyrical themes are common.
       <a href="/wiki/Cuba" title="Cuba">
        Cuban
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Colombia" title="Colombia">
        Colombian
       </a>
       , and Mexican music has infiltrated the country, especially
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Salsa_music" title="Salsa music">
         salsa
        </a>
       </i>
       and
       <i>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cumbia_music" title="Cumbia music">
         cumbia
        </a>
       </i>
       . Popular music in El Salvador uses
       <i>
        marimba
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        tehpe'ch
       </i>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Flute" title="Flute">
        flutes
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Drum" title="Drum">
        drums
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Scraper_(instrument)" title="Scraper (instrument)">
        scrapers
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Gourd" title="Gourd">
        gourds
       </a>
       , as well as more recently imported
       <a href="/wiki/Guitar" title="Guitar">
        guitars
       </a>
       and other instruments. El Salvador's well known folk dance is known as
       <i>
        Xuc
       </i>
       which originated in
       <a href="/wiki/Cojutepeque" title="Cojutepeque">
        Cojutepeque
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Cuscatl%C3%A1n_Department" title="Cuscatlán Department">
        Cuscatlan
       </a>
       . Other musical repertoire consists of danza, pasillo, marcha and canciones.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Sport">
        Sport
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Estadio_cuscatlan.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1536" data-file-width="2048" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/Estadio_cuscatlan.jpg/220px-Estadio_cuscatlan.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/Estadio_cuscatlan.jpg/330px-Estadio_cuscatlan.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/Estadio_cuscatlan.jpg/440px-Estadio_cuscatlan.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Estadio_cuscatlan.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         The
         <a href="/wiki/Estadio_Cuscatl%C3%A1n" title="Estadio Cuscatlán">
          Estadio Cuscatlán
         </a>
         in San Salvador is the largest stadium in Central America
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sport_in_El_Salvador" title="Sport in El Salvador">
        Sport in El Salvador
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">
        Football
       </a>
       is the most popular sport in El Salvador. The
       <a href="/wiki/El_Salvador_national_football_team" title="El Salvador national football team">
        El Salvador national football team
       </a>
       qualified for the
       <a href="/wiki/FIFA_World_Cup" title="FIFA World Cup">
        FIFA World Cup
       </a>
       in
       <a href="/wiki/1970_FIFA_World_Cup" title="1970 FIFA World Cup">
        1970
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/1982_FIFA_World_Cup" title="1982 FIFA World Cup">
        1982
       </a>
       . Their qualification for the 1970 tournament was marred by the
       <a href="/wiki/Football_War" title="Football War">
        Football War
       </a>
       , a war against
       <a href="/wiki/Honduras" title="Honduras">
        Honduras
       </a>
       , whose team El Salvador's had defeated.
      </p>
      <p>
       The national football team play at the
       <a href="/wiki/Estadio_Cuscatl%C3%A1n" title="Estadio Cuscatlán">
        Estadio Cuscatlán
       </a>
       in San Salvador. It opened in 1976 and seats 53,400, making it the largest stadium in Central America and the Caribbean.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-124">
        <a href="#cite_note-124">
         [124]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
